Sea Animals: The Hanafi Position and Opposing Views
Presents Hanafi position and opposing views on sea animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sea animals and explain the opposing schools' proofs from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Only fish from the sea is halal; the general permission is restricted.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents the Hanafi position that only fish is halal from sea animals. It then records the views of Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and others who permit all or most sea creatures. The opposing proofs are also cited. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between general texts (amm) and their restrictions (takhsis) in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what al-Quduri says: 'Only fish is eaten from water animals.'
This is the matn of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their positions
List the views of Malik (all sea animals halal), Shafi'i (three views: all, all except pig/dog/human, all except frog), and others.
Note the internal ikhtilaf within the Shafi'i school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof from Quran and hadith
The opponents cite Quran 5:96 ('Made lawful for you is the game of the sea') and the hadith 'Its water is purifying and its dead are halal.'
These texts are general; the dispute is about their scope.
4
Analyze the opponent's additional rational argument
The opponents argue that sea animals lack blood, which is the prohibited substance, so they resemble fish and are halal.
This is a qiyas argument.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis eat only fish; others eat all sea creatures. Same applies to selling.
The passage explicitly states 'the difference in eating and sale is one.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دریائی جانوروں میں سے کون سا جانور کھانا حلال ہے، اقوال فقہاء
كتاب الذبائح
قال ولا يوكل من حيوان الماء الا السمك وقال مالك وجماعة من اهل العلم باطلاق جميع مافي البحر واستثنى بعضهم الخنزير والكلب والانسان وعن الشافعى انه اطلق ذالک کله والخلاف فی الاكل والبيع واحد
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور پانی کے جانوروں میں مچھلی کے علاوہ کچھ نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور مالک اور اہل علم کی ایک جماعت ان تمام جانوروں کی اباحت کے قائل ہیں جو دریا میں ہیں اور ان میں سے بعض نے خنزیر اور کتے اور انسان کا استثناء کیا ہے اور شافعی سے منقول ہے کہ انہوں نے ان تمام کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور کھانے اور بیع میں اختلاف ایک ہے۔
تشریح حنفیہ کے نزدیک دریائی جانوروں میں سے صرف مچھلی جائز ہے اور کچھ جائز نہیں ہے۔
اور امام مالک، ابن ابی لیلی اور اصحاب الظواہر اور امام شافعی کے ایک قول میں دریا کا ہر جانور حلال ہے خواہ وہ دریائی خنزر پر اور کتا اور انسان ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ ہے کہ سب جانور حلال ہیں مگر دریائی خنزیر اور کتا اور انسان جائز نہیں ۔ یہی لیٹ کا قول ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کا تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مینڈک کے علاوہ سب جانور حلال ہیں۔
فریق مخالف کی دلیل
لهم قوله تعالى احل لكم صيد البحر من غير فصل وقوله عليه السلام في البحر هو الطهور ماؤه والحل ميتته ولانه لادم في هذه الاشياء اذا الدموى لايسكن الماء والمحرم هو الدم فاشبه السمك ترجمہ ان سب کی دلیل فرمانِ باری تعالیٰ احل لكم الصيد البحر ہے بغیر تفصیل کے اور دریا کے بارے میں نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اس کا پانی پاک کرنے والا ہے اور اس کا مردار حلال ہے اور اسلئے کہ ان چیزوں میں خون نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کہ خون والا پانی میں نہیں رہ سکتا اور حرام کرنے والا وہ خون ہے تو یہ سب مچھلی کے مشابہ ہو گئے ۔
تشریح یہ فریق مخالف کی دلیل ہے جو تین اجزاء پر مشتمل ہے۔ - آیت احل لكم الصيد البحر تمہارے لئے دریا کا شکار حلال کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اس میں تفصیل نہیں کہ کون سا حلال کیا گیا ہے اور کون سانہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقاً دریائی شکار حلال ہے تو اس میں سب جانور حلال ہو گئے ۔ -۲- حدیث، دریا کا پانی خوب پاک کرنے والا ہے اور اس کا مردار حلال ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ دریائی مردار حلال ہے لہذا مذکورہ تمام دریائی جانور حلال ہوں گے۔ - اصل حرام کرنے والی چیز وہ خون ہے اور دریائی جانوروں میں خون نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر ان میں خون ہوتا تو یہ پانی میں ہمیشہ نہ رہ پاتے تو یہ تو مچھلی کے حکم میں ہوں گے۔ پھر جس نے کھانے کو جائز کہا اس نے بیع کو بھی جائز کہا ہے لہذا بیع میں بھی یہی اختلاف
Among sea animals, which animal is halal to eat? Statements of jurists. Book of Slaughterings. He said: 'And nothing from water animals is eaten except fish.' And Malik and a group of scholars said all that is in the sea is permissible in absolute terms; some of them excepted pig, dog, and human. And from al-Shafi'i it is narrated that he permitted all of that absolutely. And the difference in eating and sale is one. Translation: al-Quduri said: Among water animals, nothing is eaten except fish. And Malik and a group of scholars hold the permissibility of all animals that are in the sea, and some of them excepted pig, dog, and human. And it is narrated from al-Shafi'i that he declared all of them permissible. And the difference in eating and sale is the same. Explanation: According to the Hanafis, among sea animals, only fish is permissible and nothing else is permissible. And Imam Malik, Ibn Abi Layla, the Zahiris, and in one view of Imam al-Shafi'i, every sea animal is halal, even if it is a sea pig, dog, or human. One view of Imam al-Shafi'i is that all animals are halal except sea pig, dog, and human; this is also the view of Layth. And a third view of Imam al-Shafi'i is that all animals are halal except frogs. The proof of the opposing party: They have the statement of Allah the Exalted: 'Made lawful for you is the game of the sea' without specification; and the statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding the sea: 'Its water is purifying and its dead are halal'; and because there is no blood in these things, for blooded creatures cannot live in water, and what is prohibited is blood, so they resemble fish. Explanation: This is the proof of the opposing party, consisting of three parts: 1) The verse 'Made lawful for you is the game of the sea' without distinction, so it indicates that all sea game is generally halal, including all animals. 2) The hadith that the sea's water is purifying and its dead are halal, so all dead sea animals are halal. 3) The fundamental prohibiting factor is blood, and sea animals have no blood, for if they had blood they could not live permanently in water, so they are like fish. Then, whoever allowed eating also allowed selling, so the same difference applies to sale.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute passage. The author presents the matn from al-Quduri stating the Hanafi position: only fish from sea animals is halal. Then he mentions the positions of other scholars: Malik and a group (including Ibn Abi Layla and Zahiris) permit all sea animals absolutely; some (including a view of Shafi'i) except pig, dog, and human; a third view of Shafi'i excepts frogs. The Hanafi commentary then presents the opposing proofs: the Quranic verse (5:96) which says 'game of the sea' is made lawful without specification, and the hadith that the sea's water is purifying and its dead are halal. Additionally, they argue that sea animals have no blood, which is the only thing prohibited, so they are similar to fish. The commentary explains each of these proofs in Urdu. Note that the Hanafi school's own proof against these opposing views is not given in this excerpt; the focus is on presenting the dispute and the opponents' arguments. The passage concludes that the same difference applies to selling these animals.

Key Terms
صید البحر (sayd al-bahr): Game or catch from the sea, including all sea animals.
باطلاق (bi-itlaq): In absolute terms, without any restriction or exception.
میتہ (maytah): Dead animal that has not been slaughtered; the hadith declares sea dead to be halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the matn (Quduri), which sea animals are halal to eat?
A) All sea animals except pig, dog, and human.
B) Only fish.
C) All sea animals except frogs.
D) All sea animals are halal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that only fish from the sea is halal; this ruling applies to both eating and selling.

Hanafi Ruling on Locust and Fish: No Slaughter Required
States Hanafi position on locust and fish exemption from slaughter, with Maliki counterargument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on eating locust and fish without slaughter, explain the Maliki objection, and evaluate which proof prevails.

Core Idea
Fish and locust are halal without slaughter because a hadith exempts them — nass over qiyas.

In the Hanafi school, the general requirement of ritual slaughter (dhabh) for land animals has two notable exceptions: fish and locust. This ruling is based on a prophetic hadith that declares two dead animals permissible. However, Imam Malik disagrees concerning locust, arguing by analogy to other land animals. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the Hanafi reliance on textual evidence over analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying what the Hanafi school holds regarding fish and locust: they are permissible to eat without any slaughter, alive or dead.
This applies to all types of fish and locust, as per the matn of Quduri.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Malik requires locust to be slaughtered (head cut off) before eating, analogizing it to other land animals.
The opposing school is Maliki; the issue is specific to locust, not fish.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Maliki evidence: qiyas (analogy) on the basis that locust is a land creature, and the fact that a pilgrim pays compensation for killing it, indicating it is game subject to dhabh.
This shows the Maliki method favors qiyas over the specific hadith in their view.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith 'Ahillat lana maytatan' (two dead animals made permissible) explicitly includes locust, so it is a nass (textual proof) that overrides qiyas. Compensation in ihram does not imply dhabh.
The Hanafi principle is that a specific textual ruling takes precedence over general analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi allows eating locust without any cutting; Maliki requires cutting the head. This affects daily practice and also rulings for pilgrims.
The difference is operational and matters for those following each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جریث اور بام اور مچھلی کی تمام اقسام اور ٹڈی کو بغیر زکاۃ کے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور فرمایا مالک نے کہ ٹڈی حلال نہ ہو گی مگر یہ کہ پکڑنے والا اس کا سر کاٹے اور بھونے اس لئے کہ یہ خشکی کا شکار ہے اور اس معنی کی وجہ سے محرم پر اس کے قتل کی وجہ سے ایسی جزاء ہے جو اس کے لائق ہو تو ٹڈی حلال نہ ہو گی مگر قتل کے ساتھ جیسے خشکی کے تمام جانوروں میں اور حجت مالک کے خلاف وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح مچھلی کی قسموں میں سے ایک جریث ہے جو سیاہ ہوتی ہے اور ایک مارمارہی ہے۔ جس کو بام کہتے ہیں جو سانپ کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے۔ بہر حال کوئی بھی مچھلی ہو اور ٹڈی دونوں کو بغیر ذکاۃ کے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
مگر امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ٹڈی کو ذبح کرنا پڑے گا یعنی یہ کہ اس کا سر الگ کر دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ ٹڈی خشکی کا جانور ہے اور خشکی کے تمام جانوروں میں ذکاۃ ضروی ہے تو ٹڈی میں بھی ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ ٹڈی خشکی کا جانور ہے اسی لئے تو اگر محرم نڈی کو قتل کر دے تو اس پر جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے جیسے جوں میں جزاء واجب ہوتے ہے کہ جتنا چاہے صدقہ کر دے۔ مگر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں آگیا کہ احلت لنا میتتان اس میں مچھلی اور ٹڈی دونوں داخل ہیں تو جیسے مچھلی کو غیر زکاۃ کے کھانا جائز ہے۔ ایسے ہی ٹڈی کو بھی بغیر زکاۃ کے کھانا جائز ہوگا۔
Book of Slaughterings. Translation: Quduri stated that there is no harm in eating jurith, bam, all types of fish, and locust without slaughter. Malik stated that locust is not halal unless the catcher cuts its head and roasts it, because it is a land game, and for this reason, if a pilgrim kills it, compensation is due on him, so locust is not halal except with slaughter, like all land animals. And against Malik, the evidence is the hadith which we have narrated. Commentary: Among the types of fish, one is jurith which is black, and one is marmarahi, called bam, which resembles a snake. In any case, any fish and locust can be eaten without slaughter—there is no harm. But Imam Malik says that locust must be slaughtered, i.e., its head must be separated, because locust is a land animal and slaughter is necessary for all land animals, so it will also be required for locust. And because locust is a land animal, if a pilgrim kills it, compensation is obligatory on him, like in the case of a louse. However, we say that the hadith came: 'Two dead animals are made permissible for us,' which includes both fish and locust. So just as fish can be eaten without slaughter, similarly locust will also be permissible without slaughter.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik concerning the permissibility of eating fish and locust without slaughter. The Hanafi position, based on Quduri's matn, is that all types of fish and locust are halal without any need for slaughter (dhabh). Imam Malik disagrees specifically regarding locust, arguing that since it is a land creature, it requires slaughter, analogizing it to other land animals and noting that a pilgrim (muhrim) must pay compensation for killing it. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'Ahillat lana maytatan' (Two dead animals are made halal for us), which includes fish and locust. The Hanafi rely on this textual evidence (nass) over qiyas, which is a key feature of their method. The commentary clarifies that all types of fish, including the black jurith and the eel-like bam, are included, and the hadith overrides the analogy made by Malik.

Key Terms
زكاة / ذكاة (zakat / dhaka): Here, ritual slaughter (dhabh) of animals for food
جريث (jureeth): A type of black fish mentioned in the text
بام (bam): A type of fish resembling an eel or snake
ميتتان (maytatan): Two dead animals (fish and locust) made permissible without slaughter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Chicken that died naturally
B) Locust caught alive
C) Cow that died from drowning
D) Sheep slaughtered by a non-Muslim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits eating locust and fish without slaughter based on the hadith 'Ahillat lana maytatan', overriding the qiyas requiring dhabh for land animals.

Ruling on Locust: Permissibility Even if Dead
Narration from Ali permitting locust even if dead, with contrast to fish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating locust found dead and explain the evidence from the narration of Ali (ra).

Core Idea
Locust is permissible to eat even if found dead, based on the explicit permission from Ali (ra).

This lesson examines a key narration from Ali (ra) that serves as primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling on locust. Unlike fish, where a specific exception (taafi) exists, locust remains entirely permissible regardless of how it died. The text highlights the eloquence of Ali's reply and the legal distinction between locust and fish.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Narration
Read the narration from Ali (ra) in the source: he was asked about locust mixed dead and alive, and he replied 'kulleh kulleh' (eat all of it). Recognize that this is considered a mark of eloquence.
The repetition emphasizes comprehensive permission.
2
Extract the Ruling
From this narration, the Hanafi school derives that locust is halal whether alive or dead, even if it died naturally (hatfi anfih). Note the absence of any condition requiring slaughter.
This is a specific exemption from the general rule that dead animals require proper slaughter.
3
Contrast with Fish (Taafi)
The passage contrasts locust with fish: a fish that dies without external cause (taafi) is makrooh, based on a hadith from Jabir prohibiting it. Understand that the default permissibility for dead sea creatures is qualified by this exception.
The hadith on taafi overrides the general principle that 'its dead is halal'.
4
Analyze the Analogy (Qiyas)
Some might analogize locust to fish, but the Hanafi response is that a specific text (nass) regarding locust (the narration from Ali) overrides any analogical reasoning. For fish, the restrictive text exists for taafi only.
This shows the primacy of nass over qiyas when a clear text is available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسئل على رضى الله عنه عن الجراد ياخذه الرجل من الارض وفيها الميت وغيره فقال كله كله وهذا عد من فصاحته ودل على اباحته وان مات حتف انفه بخلاف السمك اذا مات من غير آفة لانا خصصناه بالنص الوارد في الطافي
ترجمہ اور سوال کیا گیا علی سے ٹڈی کے بارے میں جس کو کوئی شخص زمین سے پکڑتا ہے کہ ان میں سے بعض مری ہوئی ہیں اور بعض اس کا غیر ہیں (یعنی زندہ ہیں ) تو آپ نے فرمایا ان تمام کو کھاؤ اور یہ علی کی فصاحت میں شمار کیا گیا ہے اور یہ ارشاد دال ہے نڈی کی اباحت پر اگر چہ وہ اپنی موت مری ہو بخلاف مچھلی کے جبکہ وہ بغیر آفت کے مر جائے اسلئے کہ ہم نے مچھلی کی تخصیص کر لی اس نص کی وجہ ے جو وارد ہوئی ہے طافی کے سلسلہ میں ۔
تشریح منڈی زندہ ہو یا مردہ سب حلال ہیں اور مچھلی کا بھی یہی حکم ہے بس صرف طافی اس حکم سے مستثنیٰ ہے کہ وہ حلال نہیں ہے۔ و الحل ميتـه کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ طافی بھی حلال ہو بالفاظ دیگر مری ہوئی مچھلی بھی حلال ہو جیسے مری ہوئی ٹڈی حلال ہے مگر کیا کریں ٹڈی کے بارے میں کوئی نص نہیں اور مچھلی کے بارے میں حدیث جابر گذر چکی ہے۔ جس میں طافی سے منع کر دیا گیا ہے اس مجبوری کی وجہ سے ہمیں مچھلی میں تخصیص کرنی پڑی۔ اور نص صرف طافی کے بارے میں وارد ہے تو اس کو ہم نے مکر وہ کہا اور باقی سب کو حلال کیا۔

۲۶۷ كتاب الذبائح اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ حضرت علی سے ان ٹڈیوں کے بارے میں پوچھا گیا کہ جن میں کچھ مردہ ہیں اور کچھ زندہ تو انہوں نے فرمایا : کله کله ان تمام کو کھاؤ تو ان کا یہ فرمان ٹڈی کی اباحت پر دال ہے اگر چہ وہ خود مری ہو۔ اور یہ جملہ حضرت علی کی فصاحت میں سے شمار کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ دو متشاکل کلموں کو جمع فرما دیا اور معنی الگ الگ ہیں۔
Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about locust which a man takes from the ground, some of which are dead and some are alive, so he said: 'Eat all of it, eat all of it.' This is counted among his eloquence, and it indicates the permissibility of locust even if it died naturally, unlike fish when it dies without a cause, because we have specified fish due to the text that came regarding al-taafi. Translation: And Ali was asked about locust... then he said: 'All of it, all of it' and this is counted among his eloquence, and this statement indicates the permissibility of locust even if it died naturally, contrary to fish when it dies without an affliction, because we have specified fish due to the text that came regarding al-taafi. Commentary: Locust, whether alive or dead, all are halal, and fish also has the same ruling, except al-taafi is excluded from this ruling, as it is not halal. The general meaning of 'its dead is halal' would require that al-taafi also be halal; in other words, dead fish should also be halal just as dead locust is halal. But what can be done? There is no text regarding locust, but regarding fish, the hadith of Jabir has passed which prohibits al-taafi. Due to this constraint, we had to specify exception for fish. And the text (nass) is only regarding al-taafi, so we declared it makrooh and considered all others as halal. [Page 268] 267 Book of Slaughterings Ashraf al-Hidayah sharh Urdu Hidayah vol 13: Hazrat Ali was asked about those locusts, some of which were dead and some alive, so he said: 'Kulleh kulleh' (Eat all of them). So this statement of his indicates the permissibility of locust even if it died on its own. And this sentence is counted among Hazrat Ali's eloquence because he joined two similar words but the meanings are separate.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage provides a narration from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) as evidence for the permissibility of eating locust even if found dead. When asked about locusts that were mixed between dead and live, Ali simply said 'kulleh kulleh' (eat all of it). The commentator notes that this is considered a mark of eloquence because he used two words that appear the same but carry different emphatic meanings. The text then makes a distinction: for locust, even death by natural cause is halal, but for fish, if it dies without an external cause (like al-taafi, which dies on its own and floats), it is not halal. This is because a specific hadith (from Jabir) prohibits al-taafi. So the general principle that dead sea creatures are halal is qualified for fish by an exception for taafi. The commentary clarifies that locust has no such restrictive text, so it remains completely permissible regardless of how it died. The distinction arises from the explicit text (nass) regarding fish, not from any inherent difference in the animals themselves.

Key Terms
كله كله (kulleh kulleh): Phrase used by Ali meaning 'all of it, all of it' - emphasizing complete permissibility
طافي (taafi): A fish that dies without external cause and floats on water; considered makrooh in Hanafi school
حتف أنفه (hatfi anfih): Dying a natural death without any external cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on eating a locust that is found dead on the ground?
A) It is not halal because it died without slaughter
B) It is halal only if it was killed by the person
C) It is halal whether it died naturally or was killed
D) It is makrooh like taafi fish

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits eating locust regardless of how it died, based on the narration of Ali, and distinguishes it from fish due to a specific hadith on taafi.

General Principle for Fish: Death by Affliction Halal, Otherwise Not
Establishes a general legal principle for fish death types and their rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) for fish permissibility, apply it to cases of taafi, cut fish, and death from heat/cold, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Fish is halal if it dies by an external cause (afa); if it dies naturally (taafi), it is not halal.

This passage establishes a fundamental rule in Hanafi fiqh for determining whether a fish is halal or makruh. The key distinction is the presence or absence of an external affliction (afa) that causes death. Understanding this principle is essential because it applies to many specific cases, such as fish caught, cut into pieces, or dying from extreme temperatures. The passage also highlights an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding heat/cold death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its categories
The text divides fish death into two categories: death by affliction (halal) and natural death (not halal). Recognize the act being evaluated: the death of a fish and its permissibility for consumption.
The categories are mutually exclusive.
2
Define the key terms
Understand 'afa' (external cause such as being caught, cut, or affected by heat/cold) and 'taafi' (natural death without external cause, fish floats).
These terms are crucial for applying the principle.
3
Apply to the cut-fish example
Trace the reasoning: cutting causes death → death is by affliction → fish and cut piece are halal. The cut piece is halal because dead sea creatures are halal (except taafi).
This example illustrates the principle's application.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf on heat/cold death
Note the two narrations: one allows (considering heat/cold as affliction), the other prohibits. Identify the preferred view (mukhtar) of permissibility.
The ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The fatwa in Majma' al-Anhur declares death from heat or cold as halal. Understand that this is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
The principle is consistent with the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الاصل في السمك عندنا انه اذا مات بافة يحل كالماخوذ واذا مات حتف انفه من غير افة لا يحل كالطافي وتنسحب عليه فروع كثيرة بيناها فى كفاية المنتهى وعند التامل يقف المبرز عليها منها اذا قطع بعضها فمات يحل اكل ما ابين وما بقى لان موته بافة وما ابين من الحى وان كان ميتافميتته حلال وفي الموت بالحر والبرد روايتان والله اعلم بالصواب
ترجمہ پھر ہمارے نزدیک مچھلی کے بارے میں قاعدہ کلیہ ہے کہ جب وہ کسی آفت سے مرے تو حلال ہے جیسے وہ جس کو پکڑ لیا گیا ہو اور جبکہ وہ بغیر آفت کے اپنی موت مرے تو وہ حلال نہیں ہے جیسے طافی اور اسی قاعدہ پر بہت فروع متفرع ہوتی ہیں جس کو ہم نے کفایتہ ہنتہی میں بیان کیا ہے اور اقف ہو جائے گا ان فروع سے وہ شخص جو فائق ہو تا مل کے وقت انہیں فروع میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ جب مچھلی کا بعض حصہ کاٹ دیا گیا پس وہ مر گئی تو جس ٹکڑے کو علیحدہ کیا گیا ہے وہ اور جو باقی رہ گیا ہے وہ حلال ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی موت آفت کی وجہ سے ہے اور جو ٹکڑا زندہ جانور سے الگ کر لیا جائے اگر چہ وہ مردار ہے پس دریا کا مردار حلال ہے اور گرمی اور سردی سے مرنے میں دور واسیتیں ہیں ، واللہ ا
تشریح مچھلی کے بارے میں یہ قاعدہ کلیہ ہے کہ جب وہ کسی آفت سے مرے تو وہ حلال ہوگی اور اگر بغیر آفت کے مرے تو وہ حلال نہیں ہوگی ۔ اول جیسے وہ مچھلی جس کو شکاری نے پکڑ لیا اور دوسری جیسے طافی مکروہ ہے۔
پھر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ایسا اصول کلی ہے جس پر فروعات کثیرہ متفرع ہوتی ہیں جن کو سمجھدار آدمی خود نکال سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً ایک مچھلی کا کچھ ٹکڑا کاٹ لیا گیا ہے جس سے وہ مرگئی تو یہ موت آفت کی وجہ سے ہے تو مچھلی بھی حلال ہے اور وہ ٹکڑا بھی حلال ہے۔ مچھلی حلال کیوں ہے؟ یہ تو ظاہر ہےاور ٹکڑا اگر چہ زندہ چیز کا ٹکڑا ہے جو حلال نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ بلکہ مردار ہوتا ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ مچھلی کا ٹکڑا ہے جو دریائی جانور ہے اور دریا کا مردار حلال ہوتا ہے۔ جو مچھلی شدت گرمی یا شدت برودت کی وجہ سے مرگئی اس میں دو قول ہیں ایک جواز کا ، دوسرے عدم جواز کا نگر مختار اول ہے۔
مجمع الانہر ص ۴۹۶ ج ۲ پر گرمی اور سردی سے مرنے والی کے بارے میں حلت پر فتوی دیا گیا ہے۔
Then the principle regarding fish according to us is that when it dies due to an affliction, it is halal, like the one caught. And when it dies naturally without an affliction, it is not halal, like al-taafi. And many branches are derived from it, which we have explained in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Upon reflection, the distinguished person will come across them. Among them: if a part of it is cut off and it dies, it is halal to eat both what is cut off and what remains, because its death is due to an affliction. And what is cut off from a live animal, even though it is dead, the dead of the sea is halal. Regarding death from heat and cold, there are two narrations. And Allah knows best. Commentary: This is the general principle regarding fish: when it dies due to an affliction, it is halal; if it dies without affliction, it is not halal. The first is like a fish caught by a hunter, the second is like al-taafi which is makrooh. Then the author says this is a comprehensive principle from which many branches are derived; an intelligent person can deduce them. For example, if a piece of fish is cut off causing it to die, then the death is due to an affliction, so the fish is halal and the piece is also halal. Why is the fish halal? That is obvious. And the piece, although it is a piece of a live animal which is usually not halal, rather it is dead meat, but because it is a piece of a sea creature, and the dead of the sea is halal. Regarding a fish that dies from extreme heat or cold, there are two opinions: one of permissibility, the other of impermissibility. The preferred view is the first. In Majma' al-Anhur, vol. 2, p. 496, a fatwa is given on the permissibility of fish dying from heat or cold.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage lays down the general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) for fish in the Hanafi school: if a fish dies due to an external affliction (afa), it is halal; if it dies without any external cause (hatfi anfih), it is not halal, and this is the case of al-taafi (fish that dies and floats). The author mentions that many subsidiary rulings (furu') branch off from this principle, and he refers to his larger work Kifayat al-Muntaha for details. One example is given: if a part of a fish is cut off while it is still alive and it dies as a result, both the cut-off piece and the remaining body are halal. The reasoning is that the death was caused by an affliction (the cutting), so it falls under the first category. Moreover, even the cut-off piece, though technically dead meat, is halal because the general rule is that the dead of the sea is halal (with the exception of taafi). Finally, the author notes an ikhtilaf for fish that die from extreme heat or cold: there are two narrations in the school. One view says it is halal (since these are afflictions), the other says it is not (since the cause is internal environmental factor). The preferred view (mukhtar) is permissibility, as confirmed by Majma' al-Anhur. This principle shows the Hanafi method of deriving rules from a core text and applying them consistently.

Key Terms
آفة (afa): External affliction or cause of death, such as being caught, cut, injured, or affected by extreme temperature
طافي (taafi): Fish that dies without external cause and floats on water; considered makrooh
ميتة البحر (mayyit al-bahr): Dead sea creatures; generally halal except for taafi

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general principle for fish in the Hanafi school, which of the following fish is NOT halal?
A) A fish that was caught in a net and died
B) A fish that dies after part of it was cut off
C) A fish that died naturally and floated to the surface (taafi)
D) A fish that died from extreme cold

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle for fish halal status hinges entirely on whether the fish died due to an external affliction (afa) or naturally (taafi).

Ruling of Udhiya (Qurbani): Wajib with Conditions and Scholarly Dispute
States the ruling and conditions of udhiya with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of udhiya, identify its conditions, and explain the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding its status.

Core Idea
Udhiya is wajib upon free, Muslim, resident, wealthy persons; but a minority consider it sunnah.

This passage opens the Book of Udhiya (Qurbani) with a definition, conditions, and ruling. It then details the well-known disagreement within the Hanafi school and with the Shafi‘i school. To grasp the ruling, you must distinguish between fard, wajib, and sunnah, and recognise the wealth threshold that triggers the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Define udhiya and its legal components
Identify the lexical and shar‘i definition of udhiya. Note the sabab (time: days of Nahr) and rukn (slaughtering a permissible animal with intention).
The definition uses 'tasmīyat al-shay’ bi-ism al-waqt'.
2
State the conditions for obligation
Extract the three conditions from the text: Islam, being a resident (muqim), and being wealthy to the sadaqat al-fitr threshold (mawsir).
Wealth is based on possible capacity (maqdūra), not available power (qudra muyassara).
3
Extract the ruling from the matn
From the matn of Quduri: udhiya is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person on the day of Adha, for himself and his young children.
The ruling is wājib, not farḍ, due to zanni evidence.
4
Map the scholarly dispute
Identify the majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, Hasan, and one narration of Abu Yusuf) holding wujub, and the minority (another narration of Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi‘i) holding sunnah mu'akkadah.
Al-Tahawi reports that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah mu'akkadah.
5
Discuss the thamarah al-khilaf
If wajib, omitting udhiya is sinful and must be performed; if sunnah, omission is not sinful but reward is lost. This also affects rulings on behalf of minor children.
The matn and majority opinion are relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاضحية
ـاب الاضحية
ترجمہ یہ کتاب قربانی کے احکام کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح ذبح اور قربانی میں عموم خصوص مطلق کی نسبت ہے، اول عام اور ثانی خاص ہے جیسے دیوان اور انسان ۔ اور عام کے بعد ہی خاص کا ذکر کرنا انسب ہے۔ اس لئے کہ عام خاص کا جز ہوتا ہے، مثلاً حیوان انسان کا جزء ہے اس لئے کہ انسان کی ماہیت حیوان ناطق ہے اور جزء طبعاً مقدم ہوتا ہے تو وضعاً بھی جزء کو مقدم کر دیا گیا ہے۔
الاضحية.. اصل میں اُفعُو لَةٌ کے وزن پر اضحویہ تھا علم الصیغہ میں ذکر کردہ قاعدہ نمبر ۱۴ کے مطابق اضحیۃ ہو گیا۔ لغت کے اعتبار سے اضحیہ اس جانور کو کہا جاتا ہے جس کو ایام انہی میں ذبح کیا جائے یعنی یہ تسمية الشئى باسم وقت کی قبیل ہے۔ اور شریعت میں اضحیہ کی تعریف یہ ہے ذبح حیوان مخصوص بنية القربة في وقت مخصوص شرائط اضحیہ (۱) اسلام (۲) مقیم ہونا ، اور اتنا مالدار ہونا جس کی وجہ سے صدقہ خطر واجب ہو سکے۔ بالفاظ دیگر قربانی کا وجوب صدقۂ فطر کے مثل ممکنہ کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ قدرت میسرہ کی وجہ سے۔ (والمفصیل فی درس الحسامی )
اور قربانی کا سبب ، وقت ہے یعنی ایام نحر اور بقول بعض راس ہے اور اس کا رکن ایسے جانور کو ذبح کرنا ہے جس کا ذبح کرنا یہاں جائز ہے کماسیاتی) لہذا مرغی وغیرہ کا یہاں ذبح کرنا تشبہ بالجوس کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہے۔ اور اس کا حکم دنیا میں واجب کی ذمہ داری سے خروج ہے اور آخر میں بہتر صحت نیت بفضل ایزدی ثواب حاصل کرنا ہے۔
قربانی کا حکم، قربانی کس پر، کب واجب ہے کس طرف سے واجب ہے
قال الاضحية واجبة على كل حر مسلم مقيم موسر فى يوم الاضحى عن نفسه وعن ولده الصغار اما الوجوب فقول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وزفر والحسن واحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف رحمهم الله وعنه انها سنة ذكره في الجوامع وهو قول الشافعى وذكر الطحاوى ان على قول ابي حنيفة واجبة وعلى قول ابى يوسف ومحمد سنة مؤكدة وهكذا ذكر بعض المشائخ الاختلاف
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ قربانی کرنا واجب ہے ہر ایسے آزاد پر جو مسلمان ہو مقیم ہو مالدار ہو یوم الاضح میں اپنی طرف سے اور اپنے چھوٹے بچوں کی طرف سے بہر حال وجوب پس ابو حنیفہ اور محمد اور زفر اور حسن کا قول ہے اور دو روایتوں میں سے ایک روایت ہے ابو یوسف سے اور ابو یوسف ہی سے دوسری روایت ہے کہ یہ سنت ہے جس کو ابو یوسف نے (اپنی کتاب ) جوامع میں ذکر کیا ہے اور یہی شافعی کا قول ہے اور طحاوی نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ ابو حنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق واجب ہے اور ابو یوسف اور محمد کے نزدیک پر سنت مؤکدہ ہے اور ایسے ہی بعض مشائخ نے اختلاف کو ذکر کیا ہے۔
The Book of Udhiya. Chapter of Udhiya. Translation: This book is about the rulings of sacrifice. Explanation: Between slaughter and sacrifice there is a relationship of absolute generality and specificity; the first is general and the second is specific, like animal and human. And it is more appropriate to mention the specific after the general, because the general is a part of the specific. For example, animal is a part of human, because the essence of human is rational animal, and the part is naturally prior, so it has been made prior also by convention. Al-udhiya: Originally it was ‘udhuyā on the pattern of ‘uf‘ūlatun, then according to rule no. 14 mentioned in the science of morphology it became ‘udhiyah. Lexically, udhiya is used for the animal that is slaughtered during the days of an-nahr; this is from the category of naming a thing after the name of its time. In the Shariah, the definition of udhiya is: slaughtering a specific animal with the intention of worship at a specific time. Conditions of udhiya: (1) Islam, (2) being a resident, (3) being wealthy to the extent that sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory. In other words, the obligation of sacrifice is due to possible capacity (maqdūra) like sadaqat al-fitr, not due to available power (qudra muyassara). And the cause of sacrifice is the time, i.e., the days of an-nahr, and according to some, it is the head (ras). Its rukn is to slaughter an animal that is permissible to slaughter here. Therefore, slaughtering chickens etc. here is makruh due to imitation of the Magians. Its ruling in this world is the discharge of the obligation (wajib), and in the Hereafter it is to obtain reward with good intention by the grace of God. The ruling of sacrifice, upon whom, when it is wajib, on whose behalf it is wajib. He said: Udhiya is wajib upon every free Muslim resident wealthy person on the day of Adha for himself and for his young children. As for the obligation: it is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan, and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And from him (Abu Yusuf) that it is sunnah; he mentioned it in al-Jawami‘, and it is the saying of al-Shafi‘i. And al-Tahawi mentioned that according to Abu Hanifa's saying it is wajib, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is sunnah mu'akkadah. And similarly some mashayikh mentioned the disagreement. Translation: Quduri said that sacrifice is wajib upon every free person who is Muslim, resident, wealthy, on the day of Adha, on his own behalf and on behalf of his young children. In any case, the obligation is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan, and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf, and from Abu Yusuf himself another narration that it is sunnah, which he mentioned in his book al-Jawami‘, and that is the saying of al-Shafi‘i. And al-Tahawi mentioned that according to Abu Hanifa's saying it is wajib, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and similarly some mashayikh mentioned the disagreement.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Adhiya (Book of Udhiya/Qurbani). The author first provides a lexical and shar‘i definition: udhiya is the slaughter of a specific animal with the intention of worship during a specific time (the days of Nahr). The conditions for obligation are then stated: Islam, being a resident (muqim), and possessing wealth (mawsir) to the extent that sadaqat al-fitr is wajib. The cause (sabab) of obligation is the time, and the rukn is slaughtering a permissible animal. The text then presents the central ruling from the matn of Quduri: udhiya is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person on the day of Adha for himself and for his young children. Following this, the commentary lays out the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute. The majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, Hasan ibn Ziyad, and one narration from Abu Yusuf) hold it to be wajib. Another narration from Abu Yusuf, which is also the view of Imam al-Shafi‘i, holds it to be sunnah. Al-Tahawi confirms that according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage thus demonstrates the classical Hanafi position that udhiya is a distinct obligation (wajib, not fard) due to its evidence being of zanni nature, and it highlights the well-known ikhtilaf within the school and with the Shafi‘i madhhab.

Key Terms
الاضحية (al-udhiya): The animal slaughtered during the days of Nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah) with the intention of worship, or the act of such slaughter.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation, a ruling that demands performance with a binding command, established by zanni (probable) evidence.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah, an act regularly performed by the Prophet ﷺ and emphasized, but below wajib in legal force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of udhiya for a free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person?
A) Farḍ
B) Wājib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Udhiya is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person, as held by the majority of the Hanafi school, but a legitimate minority consider it sunnah mu'akkadah.

Definition and Conditions of Udhiyah
Defining udhiyah and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of udhiyah and identify its conditions of obligation.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is wajib upon the resident Muslim who possesses the nisab of sadaqat al-fitr.

This passage opens the Book of Udhiyah. It defines the term linguistically and legally, then lists the conditions that trigger its obligation. Understanding these conditions is essential before studying the detailed rulings of sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and shar'i definitions
Find the definition of udhiyah in the text: linguistically it is named after the time, and in Shari'ah it is slaughtering a specific animal with intention of qurbah in a specific time.
The specific animal is a permissible livestock (sheep, cow, camel).
2
Extract the conditions (shurut) for obligation
The text lists three conditions: Islam, being a resident (muqim), and having wealth equal to the nisab of sadaqat al-fitr.
The condition of wealth is based on capability (mumkinah), not actual ability (qudrah mayassirah).
3
Distinguish sabab (cause) from rukn (pillar)
The sabab is the time (days of Nahr). The rukn is the slaughter of a permissible animal with intention.
The rukn is the essential act; omission invalidates. The sabab triggers the obligation.
4
Note the ruling and cross-madhhab dispute
The ruling is wajib. However, the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah mu'akkadah.
The Hanafi position is based on specific proofs (not detailed here).

اور قربانی کا سبب ، وقت ہے یعنی ایام نحر اور بقول بعض راس ہے اور اس کا رکن ایسے جانور کو ذبح کرنا ہے جس کا ذبح کرنا یہاں جائز ہے کماسیاتی) لہذا مرغی وغیرہ کا یہاں ذبح کرنا تشبہ بالجوس کی وجہ سے مکروہ ہے۔ اور اس کا حکم دنیا میں واجب کی ذمہ داری سے خروج ہے اور آخر میں بہتر صحت نیت بفضل ایزدی ثواب حاصل کرنا ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 13, page 269. The Book of Udhiyah. Translation: This book is about the rulings of sacrifice. Explanation: Slaughter (dhabh) and sacrifice (udhiyah) have a general-specific absolute relationship; the first is general, the second is specific, like Diwan and human. And it is more appropriate to mention the specific after the general, because the general is a part of the specific, e.g., animal is a part of human because the essence of human is rational animal, and the part is naturally prior, so by convention the part is also placed first. Al-Udhiyah: originally it was 'udhawiyah' on the pattern of 'uf'uulah', then it became 'udhiyah' according to rule no. 14 mentioned in morphology. Linguistically, udhiyah is an animal slaughtered during the days of Nahr; it is naming something after the name of time. In Shari'ah, the definition of udhiyah is: slaughtering a specific animal with the intention of drawing near to Allah in a specific time. Conditions of udhiyah: (1) Islam, (2) being a resident, and (3) having such wealth that sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory. In other words, the obligation of sacrifice is due to capability (mumkinah) like sadaqat al-fitr, not due to available power (qudrah mayassirah). (Al-Mufassal fi dars al-Hasami) And its cause is time, i.e., the days of Nahr; according to some, it is the head (of the year). And its rukn is to slaughter an animal whose slaughter is permissible here (like sheep, cow, camel). Therefore, slaughtering chicken etc. here is makruh because of resembling the Magians. And its ruling in this world is fulfillment of the obligation, and in the Hereafter is attainment of reward through good intention by Allah's grace.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Udhiyah (sacrifice). The commentator begins by distinguishing between general sacrifice (dhabh) and specific sacrifice (udhiyah), noting that udhiyah is a specific form of slaughter. He then provides a linguistic and shar'i definition of udhiyah: it is a specific animal slaughtered during the days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) with the intention of qurbah. The conditions for udhiyah being obligatory are: Islam, being a resident (muqim), and possessing wealth that reaches the nisab threshold for sadaqat al-fitr. The cause (sabab) of its obligation is the time (the days of Nahr), and the rukn (pillar) is slaughtering a permissible animal. The act is wajib, and failure to perform it without excuse entails sin. The commentator also notes that slaughtering poultry or birds in this context is makruh due to resemblance to Magian practices. The ruling is presented without detailed proofs here, serving as an introduction.

Key Terms
الاضحية (al-udhiyah): A specific animal sacrificed during the days of Nahr with the intention of drawing near to Allah.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation of udhiyah, which is the time (days of Nahr).
ركن (rukn): The essential act of udhiyah, which is the slaughter of a permissible animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wealth beyond nisab
B) The days of Nahr

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah is wajib upon the resident Muslim with nisab, and its cause is the days of Nahr.

Udhiyah: The Wajib vs Sunnah Dispute
Presenting the matn on udhiyah's obligation and the arguments for it being sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on udhiyah, identify the intra-Hanafi and Shafi'i disagreements, and analyze the sunnah side's hadith-based proof.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is wajib according to the fatwa, but the dispute hinges on a hadith conditioned on intention and qiyas with financial duties.

The legal status of udhiyah (sacrifice) is a matter of scholarly debate. This lesson presents the core ruling from Imam Quduri's matn, the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab ikhtilaf, and the first set of proofs from those who consider it sunnah. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the hadith and qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling from the Matn
Identify the act (udhiyah) and its hukm level as stated by Quduri: wajib. Note the conditions: free, Muslim, resident, wealthy, on the day of Adha.
The matn is definitive, but the later dispute shows it is the relied-upon position.
2
Identify the Ikhtilaf
Recognize that Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan say wajib; Abu Yusuf has two narrations (one wajib, one sunnah); al-Shafi'i says sunnah. Al-Tahawi reports that Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say sunnah mu'akkadah.
This is both an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the Sunnah Side's Naqli Proof
Read the hadith: 'Whoever intends to sacrifice, let him not cut his hair or nails.' Understand the argument: conditioning on intention (irādah) negates obligation because obligation is not conditional on desire.
The hadith is considered zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Examine the Sunnah Side's Aqli Proof
Analyze the qiyas: financial duties (e.g., zakat) are equal for resident and traveler. Since udhiyah is not wajib on traveler, it cannot be wajib on resident. Analogy with 'atirah (which is sunnah) supports this.
The qiyas uses equality in 'waza'if maliyyah'.
5
Note the Fatwa and Expectation of Hanafi Response
Despite these proofs, the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is wujub. The Hanafi response to these arguments will follow in later passages.
The student should recognize that the passage only presents one side; the full picture requires both.

Ruling of sacrifice, on whom it is wajib, when it is wajib, on whose behalf it is wajib. He (Quduri) said: Udhiyah is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person on the day of Adha, for himself and for his young children. As for the obligation (wujub), it is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Hasan, and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them). And from him (Abu Yusuf) there is another narration that it is sunnah, which he mentioned in al-Jawami', and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Al-Tahawi mentioned that according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is sunnah mu'akkadah. Thus some of the mashayikh mentioned the ikhtilaf. Translation: Quduri said that performing sacrifice is wajib upon every free person who is Muslim, resident, wealthy on the day of Adha, for himself and for his young children. In any case, the wujub is the saying of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Hasan, and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf there is another narration that it is sunnah, which he mentioned in his book al-Jawami', and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Al-Tahawi mentioned that according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and similarly some mashayikh mentioned the ikhtilaf. Explanation: This is the text of Imam Quduri, in which it is stated that sacrifice is wajib, then it is stated on whom it is wajib, then when it is wajib, then on whose behalf it is wajib. So these are four sections, which the author of Hidayah discusses in detail. In this passage, only the first discussion is mentioned. The first discussion: sacrifice is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and also one narration from Abu Yusuf. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and the second narration from Abu Yusuf, which he mentioned in al-Jawami', sacrifice is sunnah. Some mashayikh mentioned the ikhtilaf. But Imam al-Tahawi and some other mashayikh mentioned it such that according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib and according to the Sahibayn it is sunnah mu'akkadah. In any case, the fatwa is upon the obligation (wujub) of sacrifice. So here there are two opinions: (1) sunnah, (2) wujub. Now the author of Hidayah will present the proofs of each party; first he will mention the proofs of those who say it is sunnah, then the proofs of those who say it is wajib. Thus he says: Proofs of those who say sacrifice is sunnah, both naqli and aqli. The aspect of sunnah: His (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever among you intends to sacrifice, let him not take anything from his hair and nails.' Conditioning it upon intention negates obligation. And because if it were wajib upon the resident, it would be wajib upon the traveler, because they do not differ in financial duties (waza'if maliyyah) like zakat, and it becomes like 'atirah. Translation: The proof of sunnah is the Prophet's statement: 'Whoever among you intends to sacrifice, let him not take anything from his hair and nails.' Attaching it to intention negates obligation. And because if sacrifice were wajib upon the resident, it would be wajib upon the traveler, since these two do not differ in financial duties like zakat, and it became like 'atirah. Explanation: The author has mentioned two proofs of those who say sunnah: one naqli, the other aqli. The naqli proof is the mentioned hadith, in which it is said that whoever intends to sacrifice should not cut his hair etc., thus the sacrifice is conditioned upon intention, and these are not words of obligation. The aqli proof: in financial worship, resident and traveler are equal, yet sacrifice is not wajib upon the traveler. So it is known that it is also not wajib upon the resident, otherwise the ruling would differ between the two. For example, zakat is a financial worship; as it is wajib upon the resident, so too it is wajib upon the traveler. And just as 'atirah is not wajib upon the traveler, so it is not wajib upon the resident. In zakat there is equality in obligation, and in 'atirah there is equality in non-obligation, so there must be equality in sacrifice, and that would be by calling it sunnah for both, not by saying it is wajib upon the resident and not upon the traveler.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage presents the core dispute on the legal status of udhiyah. The commentator begins by quoting Quduri's matn, which states that udhiyah is wajib upon specific individuals. He then explains that this ruling is attributed to Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad, with one narration from Abu Yusuf. However, there is a second narration from Abu Yusuf (recorded in his al-Jawami') that it is sunnah, and this is also the position of Imam al-Shafi'i. Al-Tahawi reports that Abu Hanifa says wajib, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say sunnah mu'akkadah. The commentator clarifies that the fatwa (operative ruling) is on wujub, i.e., it is wajib. Then the author of Hidayah begins to present the proofs for each side, starting with the proponents of sunnah. They give two proofs: (1) The hadith 'Whoever intends to sacrifice, let him not cut his hair or nails' – conditioning on intention indicates it is not obligatory, because obligation is not conditional on intention. (2) Qiyas: if it were wajib on residents, it would be wajib on travelers, since financial duties (like zakat) are equal for both. But it is not wajib on travelers, so it is not wajib on residents either; it is like 'atirah (a pre-Islamic practice that was sunnah). The passage thus sets up the opposition's case before the Hanafi response (which follows later).

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): Obligation: the legal status that requires performance; omission is sinful.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized sunnah: a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omitting it without excuse is blameworthy but not sinful.
عتيرة ('atirah): A pre-Islamic practice of sacrificing an animal during Rajab; later abrogated or considered sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis of the sunnah side's first proof (naqli)?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) A hadith conditioning sacrifice on intention
C) Consensus of the Sahaba
D) Analogy with zakat

Key Takeaway
Despite the persuasive arguments for sunnah, the Hanafi fatwa upholds wujub (obligation) of udhiyah for the eligible Muslim.

12 min
Dispute on Udhiyah: Wajib or Sunnah?
Presents the inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of udhiyah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds udhiyah as wajib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A severe threat only attaches to leaving a wajib act — thus udhiyah is wajib.

This lesson dives into one of the most well-known inter-madhhab disputes: is the Eid sacrifice (udhiyah) obligatory or merely a highly recommended sunnah? The Hanafi school, based on a powerful hadith threat and a unique linguistic argument, considers it wajib. The Shafi'i school, and even some early Hanafi authorities, argue it is sunnah. We will walk through the proofs on both sides, understand the Hanafi response, and see why the fatwa is on wujub.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of udhiyah according to the majority of the Hanafi school, including the mufta bihi position.
The fatwa is on wujub, though some Sahibayn narrations say sunnah.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
State the Shafi'i position (and the narration from Abu Yusuf) that udhiyah is sunnah mu'akkadah, and list their main proofs: the hadith conditioning sacrifice on intention and the rational analogy to zakat and 'atirah.
The conditioning on intention ('whoever intends...') is argued to negate obligation.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the opponent's proof
Explain how the Hanafi school refutes each opposing proof: the conditioning hadith is about cutting hair, not about the ruling itself; and travel exemptions exist in financial duties like Jumu'ah, so udhiyah is analogous to Jumu'ah, not zakat.
The threat hadith is stronger evidence and only applies to wajib acts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi's own proofs
Examine the Hanafi proofs: the hadith of severe threat ('whoever finds capacity and does not sacrifice...') and the linguistic argument from 'Yawm al-Adha' indicating obligation through addition of time.
The threat is so severe it cannot be for leaving a non-obligatory act.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence: a Hanafi Muslim must perform udhiyah if able; a Shafi'i may omit it without sin. This affects fatwa and practice.
The difference is not merely theoretical but has real ritual implications.

دلیل عقلی اضافت کے ساتھ یوم الاضحی بولتے ہیں یعنی قربانی کی جانب وقت قربانی کی اضافت کرتے ہوئے۔ اور یہ اضافت اختصاص کے لئے ہے یعنی یہ شخص ہے قربانی کے ساتھ اختصاص اس وقت ثابت ہو گا کہ قربانی کا وجود ہو اور ہو سکتا ہے کہ سنت کی صورت میں تمام مکلفین ترک قربانی پر اتفاق کرلیں (جس کو مصنف نے جنس مکلفین سے تعبیر کیا ہے لہذا وجود قربانی کے لئے وجوب ضروری ہوا تا کہ اختصاص ثابت ہو سکے جیسے یوم الجمعه وقت الظهر ، شهر رمضان کے اندر یہی بات ہے۔ مسافر پر واجب نہ ہونے کی وجہ : کیوں کہ قربانی کے لئے کچھ اسباب ہونے ضروری ہیں اور مسافر کو ان اسباب کا مہیا کرتا بسا اوقات بھاری پڑ سکتا ہے نیز قربانی کے مخصوص ایام ہیں اگر وہ ایام گزر گئے تو قربانی فوت ہو جاتی ہے۔ تو ہم نے جمعہ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے مسافر کو قربانی کو واجب نہیں کیا جیسے مسافر پر جمعہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ تنبیہ وجاج کرام مٹی میں مسافر ہیں ان پر قربانی واجب نہ ہوگی البتہ تمتع در قران کرنے والوں پر دم تمتع اور دم قران واجب ہے۔
Book of Udhiyah. 20. Ashraf al-Hidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 13. Explanation: This is the text of Imam Quduri in which it is stated that sacrifice is wajib, then it is stated upon whom it is wajib, then when it is wajib, then on whose behalf it is wajib. So there are a total of four sections, which the author of Hidayah is discussing in detail. In this passage only the first discussion is mentioned. The first discussion: Sacrifice according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad is wajib, and there is also a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf to this effect. And according to Imam Shafi'i and the other narration of Imam Abu Yusuf which he mentioned in his Jami', sacrifice is sunnah. Some mashayikh have mentioned the disagreement. But Imam Tahawi and some other mashayikh have mentioned it thus: according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is wajib, and according to the Sahibayn it is sunnah mu'akkadah. In any case, the fatwa is upon the wujub of sacrifice. So here there are two opinions: 1. Sunnah, 2. Wujub. Now the author of Hidayah will present the proofs of each party: first the proofs of those who say sunnah, then the proofs of those who say wajib, as he says: Proofs of those who say sacrifice is sunnah, textual and rational proof: The basis of sunnah: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever among you intends to sacrifice, let him not take anything from his hair and nails.' And conditioning upon intention negates wujub. And because if it were wajib upon the resident, it would be wajib upon the traveler, since they do not differ in financial duties like zakat, and it becomes like the 'atirah. Translation: The proof of sunnah is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Whoever among you intends to sacrifice, let him not cut his hair and nails.' And conditioning upon intention is contrary to wujub. And because if sacrifice were wajib upon the resident, it would be wajib upon the traveler, because they do not differ in financial duties, and it becomes like the 'atirah. Explanation: The author has mentioned two proofs for those who say sunnah: one textual, one rational. The textual proof is this hadith in which it is said that whoever intends to sacrifice should not cut his hair etc., so he has conditioned sacrifice on intention, and these are not words of wujub. Rational proof: In financial worship, resident and traveler are equal, yet sacrifice is not wajib upon the traveler. So it is learned that it is also not wajib upon the resident, otherwise their rulings would differ. Like zakat is a financial worship, as it is wajib upon the resident, so too it is wajib upon the traveler. And just as 'atirah is not wajib upon the traveler, so it is not wajib upon the resident. In zakat there is equality in wujub, and in 'atirah there is equality in non-wujub, so in sacrifice there should also be equality, and that will be by considering it sunnah in both cases, not that it is wajib upon the resident and not upon the traveler. The author himself will later state that 'atirah is a goat that was slaughtered in the month of Rajab in the time of ignorance; Islam abrogated it, so ponder. Proof of the wujub of sacrifice: And the basis of wujub: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever finds capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our place of prayer.' And such a threat does not attach to leaving something non-obligatory. And because it is an act of worship to which its time is added; it is said 'Yawm al-Adha', and that indicates wujub, because addition is for specification, and specification is with existence, and wujub is that which leads to existence apparently considering the genus (of obligated persons). However, performance is specified with causes whose procurement is difficult for the traveler, and it is lost with the passing of time, so it is not wajib upon him, like Jumu'ah. Translation: The proof of wujub is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Whoever finds capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not come near our Eidgah.' And such a threat does not affix to leaving something non-obligatory. And because it is a worship to which its time (the word 'yawm') is added; it is said 'Yawm al-Adha', and this indicates wujub, because addition is for specification, and specification will be with existence, and wujub is that which leads to existence apparently considering the genus of obligated persons. Apart from the fact that performance is specified with causes whose procurement is difficult for the traveler, and it is lost with the passing of time, so it is not wajib upon him, in the category of Jumu'ah. Explanation: This is the proof of those who say wujub, which includes a hadith and a rational proof, and the reason for it not being wajib upon the traveler is mentioned. The hadith: Whoever has the capacity for sacrifice and still does not sacrifice, let him not come near our Eidgah. This is a severe threat, which can only occur for leaving an obligatory act, so from this wujub is established. Rational proof: They say 'Yawm al-Adha' with addition, i.e., adding the time of sacrifice to the act of sacrifice. And this addition is for specification, i.e., this person has specification with sacrifice; this specification will be established when sacrifice exists. And it is possible that in the case of sunnah, all obligated persons might agree to leave sacrifice (which the author expressed as 'genus of obligated persons'), therefore for the existence of sacrifice, wujub is necessary so that specification can be established, like the case of Yawm al-Jumu'ah (for Zuhr) and the month of Ramadan. Reason for not being wajib upon the traveler: Because for sacrifice, some causes need to exist, and procuring those causes may sometimes be difficult for the traveler. Also, sacrifice has specific days; if those days pass, sacrifice is lost. So we analogized it to Jumu'ah and did not make sacrifice wajib upon the traveler, just as Jumu'ah is not wajib upon the traveler. Note: The noble mujahideen are travelers in the path of Allah; sacrifice will not be wajib upon them. However, those performing Tamattu' or Qiran must offer the dam of tamattu' and dam of qiran.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of udhiyah (sacrifice). The author first clarifies the positions: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, Imam Zufar, and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and one narration of Imam Abu Yusuf, udhiyah is wajib. According to Imam Shafi'i and another narration of Imam Abu Yusuf (mentioned in his Jami'), it is sunnah. Some mashayikh, including Imam Tahawi, state that Abu Hanifa says wajib while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say sunnah mu'akkadah. The relied-upon fatwa is on wujub. Then the author presents the proofs for the sunnah position: first a hadith conditioning sacrifice on intention ('Whoever intends to sacrifice, let him not cut his hair...') which indicates non-obligation, and a rational argument equating resident and traveler in financial worship (like zakat must be equal, so if traveler is not obligated, resident should not be either, analogizing to 'atirah which is not wajib on either). The author then presents the proofs for the wujub position: a hadith threatening severe punishment for not sacrificing despite capacity—such threat only accompanies wajib acts—and a rational argument from the common expression 'Yawm al-Adha' (Day of Sacrifice), where the addition of the time to the act indicates obligation because specification requires existence, and existence requires obligation. The traveler is exempted because preparation is difficult and time is limited, analogous to Jumu'ah which is also not wajib on travelers. The passage concludes by noting that mujahideen (travellers) are exempt, but those performing Tamattu' or Qiran must offer specific sacrificial animals.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of Eid al-Adha (10th-12th of Dhul Hijjah) as an act of worship.
العتيرة (al-'atirah): A sheep sacrificed in Rajab during Jahiliyyah, later abrogated in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of udhiyah (sacrifice)?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah, as per the Sahibayn
B) Wajib, based on the hadith of severe threat
C) Fard, because it is a pillar of Islam
D) Mubah, optional without reward or punishment

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah is wajib in the Hanafi school based on the severe threat hadith and the principle that such a threat only applies to leaving a wajib act.

6 min
Proof of Obligation of Sacrifice
Establishes wujub of udhiyyah via hadith and rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith and rational arguments that establish the wujub of udhiyyah and explain why Hanafis classify it as wajib rather than fard or sunnah.

Core Idea
A severe threat (wa'id) proves obligation; sacrifice is wajib, not sunnah.

Is the 'Id sacrifice (udhiyyah) obligatory or merely recommended? The Hanafi school holds it as wajib, relying on a powerful hadith and a linguistic argument. This lesson unpacks those proofs and explains why the traveler is exempt, analogous to the Friday prayer. Understanding these proofs clarifies the school's method of deriving rulings from ahad hadith and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is udhiyyah (sacrifice on 'Id al-Adha). The Hanafi ruling is wajib (obligatory) upon the resident who has nisab.
Wajib means necessary; omission without excuse is sinful.
2
Analyse the primary proof: the hadith with wa'id
The Prophet said: 'Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our musalla.' The severe threat ('fala yaqrabanna') is attached to leaving the sacrifice.
Such a threat is only applied to abandoning an obligatory act, not a recommended one.
3
Understand the implication of wa'id
In Hanafi usul, a severe threat (wa'id) indicates that the abandoned act is wajib. Since the hadith is ahad, the ruling is wajib, not fard.
Fard requires qat'i proof; ahad hadith gives zann, yielding wujub.
4
Examine the secondary proof: idafah (grammatical attribution)
The phrase 'Yawm al-Adha' (Day of Sacrifice) attributes the day to the sacrifice. This specification indicates that the sacrifice is an integral part of the day, implying obligation.
If it were not obligatory, it might be omitted, defeating the specification.
5
Understand the exception for the traveler via qiyas
Udhiyyah is not wajib on the traveler because the means are hard to procure, and the time passes quickly. Analogous to Jumu'ah prayer, which is also not obligatory on the traveler due to hardship.
This shows that wujub is conditioned upon being resident and having means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه الوجوب قوله عليه السلام من وجد سعة ولم يضح فلا يقربن مصلانا ومثل هذا الوعيد لا يلحق بترك غير الواجب ولانها قربة يضاف اليها وقتها يقال يوم الاضحى وذلك يوذن بالوجوب لان الاضافة للاختصاص وهو بالوجود والوجوب هو المفضى الى الوجود ظاهرا بالنظر الى الجنس غير ان الاداء يختص باسباب يشق على المسافر استحضارها ويفوت بمضى الوقت فلا تجب عليه بمنزلة الجمعة
And the proof of obligation is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever has capacity and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our place of prayer.' And such a threat does not attach to the abandonment of a non-obligatory act. And because it is an act of worship to which its time is added; it is said 'the day of sacrifice', and that indicates obligation, because addition is for specification, and specification occurs through existence, and obligation is what leads to existence, apparently in consideration of the class (of obligated persons). However, performance is specific to causes whose procurement is difficult for the traveler, and it is lost with the passing of the time, so it is not obligatory upon him, like the Friday prayer.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage presents the primary evidence for the obligation (wujub) of udhiyyah (sacrifice) in the Hanafi madhhab. It first cites a hadith: 'Whoever has the means and does not sacrifice, let him not approach our musalla (place of 'Id prayer).' Such a severe threat is only attached to abandoning an obligatory act, not a recommended one. Second, a rational argument: the term 'day of sacrifice' (yawm al-adha) attributes the day to the sacrifice, indicating specification and hence obligation. Without obligation, the act might not be performed, negating the specification. The passage then explains why the traveler is exempt: the means of sacrifice are hard for him to secure, and the time is short; analogously to Jumu'ah, which is also not obligatory on the traveler.

Key Terms
الاضحية (al-udhiyyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of 'Id al-Adha as an act of worship.
الوعيد (al-wa'id): A severe threat of punishment, indicating the act is obligatory.
الاضافة (al-idafah): Grammatical attribution: attributing the day to the sacrifice demonstrates specification and obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider the sacrifice (udhiyyah) as wajib (obligatory) rather than merely sunnah?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands it.
B) Because the hadith 'Whoever has capacity... let him not approach our musalla' contains a severe threat, which only accompanies abandonment of an obligatory act.
C) Because the Sahaba unanimously agreed on its obligation.
D) Because it is sacrificial, and all sacrifices are wajib.

Key Takeaway
Udhiyyah is wajib upon the resident who has means; the proof is a hadith with a severe threat and the grammatical attribution of the day to the sacrifice.

Conditions for Obligation of Sacrifice
Lists five conditions for udhiyyah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five conditions for the obligation of udhiyyah and explain the rationale for each.

Core Idea
Udhiyyah is wajib only on a free, Muslim, resident with nisab, and within its appointed time.

This passage from Al-Hidayah lays out the five conditions that trigger the obligation (wujub) of udhiyyah. Understanding these conditions is essential for determining who must sacrifice and when. Each condition is derived from the nature of the act as a financial worship (ibadah maliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Recognize that udhiyyah is a financial act of worship with specific conditions for obligation, not for validity.
The passage deals with shurut al-wujub, not shurut al-sihhah.
2
Extract each condition and its rationale
For each condition listed, note the brief reasoning given: freedom (ownership), Islam (worship), residency (exemption for travelers), wealth (capacity), time (specific days).
The measure of wealth is the nisab of sadaqat al-fitr, as previously mentioned in the book of fasting.
3
Apply the conditions to a hypothetical
Take a concrete person and check each condition: free? Muslim? Resident? Has nisab? Is it the time?
If any condition is lacking, the act is not wajib.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note that Shafi'is do not require freedom or residency and consider udhiyyah sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
This ikhtilaf affects the binding nature of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانما اختص الوجوب بالحرية لانها وظيفة مالية لاتتادى الا بالملك والمالك هو الحر وبالاسلام لكونها قربة وبالاقامة لما بينا واليسار لما روينا من اشتراط السعة ومقداره ما يجب به صدقة الفطر وقد مر في الصوم والوقت وهو يوم الاضحى لانها مختصة به وسنبين مقدارة ان شاء الله تعالى
And obligation is specific to freedom because it is a financial duty that is only fulfilled through ownership, and the owner is the free person; and to Islam because it is an act of worship; and to residency for what we have explained; and to wealth because of what we have narrated regarding the condition of capacity, and its measure is what necessitates sadaqat al-fitr, and it has passed in [the book of] fasting; and to time, and that is the day of sacrifice, because it is specific to it, and we will explain its measure if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions for the obligation (wujub) of udhiyyah. Five conditions are listed: (1) Freedom: because udhiyyah is a financial act requiring ownership; only a free person can fully own property. (2) Islam: because it is an act of worship, and worship is not accepted from a non-Muslim. (3) Residency (al-iqamah): as previously explained, the traveler is exempt due to hardship. (4) Wealth (al-yasar): the same threshold as sadaqat al-fitr (nisab, roughly 200 dirhams or equivalent in cash/goods), which was mentioned in the chapter on fasting. (5) Time: the days of sacrifice (10th-13th of Dhul Hijjah); the sacrifice must be performed within this time. The correct measure of time will be explained later.

Key Terms
الحرية (al-hurriyyah): Freedom from slavery; a condition for obligation of financial duties requiring ownership.
اليسار (al-yasar): Financial capacity measured by the nisab of sadaqat al-fitr (200 dirhams or equivalent).
الاقامة (al-iqamah): Being a resident (muqim), not a traveler on a journey of three days or more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of udhiyyah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Being free (hurr)
B) Being a Muslim
C) Being a traveler (musafir)
D) Possessing the nisab of sadaqat al-fitr

Key Takeaway
Udhiyyah is wajib only when all five Hanafi conditions (freedom, Islam, residency, nisab, time) are met; missing even one lifts the obligation.
