Hanafi Position on 'Irada' and the 'Atirah Analogy
Hanafi response to opposing school's hadith interpretation and abrogation of 'Atirah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school interprets 'irada' in the sacrifice hadith as resolve (not choice) and why analogy to 'Atirah is rejected.

Core Idea
Irada in the hadith means resolve (qasd), not choice; abrogated 'Atirah cannot form a valid analogy.

This lesson unpacks a crucial Hanafi response to an opposing school's interpretation of a hadith about sacrifice. At stake is whether the prohibition on cutting hair before sacrifice is obligatory or merely recommended. The Hanafi commentator clarifies the meaning of 'irada' and refutes an analogy to the pre-Islamic practice of 'Atirah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine what exactly is in dispute: the interpretation of the word 'irada' in the hadith about one intending to sacrifice, and the validity of using 'Atirah as an analogy.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that 'irada' means firm intention (qasd), not choice. Therefore, the prohibition on cutting hair is wajib for anyone who intends to sacrifice.
This is based on the usul principle that 'irada' in commands indicates determination.
3
Present the opposing school's view
The opposing school (likely Shafi'i) interprets 'irada' as giving choice, so the prohibition is merely recommended (sunnah). They also analogize to 'Atirah, a pre-Islamic practice of slaughtering in Rajab.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof and rebuttal
The Hanafi proof: analogous commands like 'Whoever intends to pray, let him perform wudu' show 'irada' implies obligation of prerequisites. The rebuttal to the 'Atirah analogy: 'Atirah is abrogated, and abrogated rulings cannot be used for qiyas.
The commentator stresses that using 'irada' to deduce sunnah is incorrect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi holds it is wajib to refrain from cutting hair from 1st Dhul-Hijjah until the sacrifice; the opposing school considers it merely recommended.
This affects whether cutting hair is a sin (Hanafi) or not (other).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فریق مخالف کی حدیث کا جواب
والمراد بالارادة فيماروى والله اعلم ماهو ضد السهو لا التخيير والعتيرة منسوخة وهي شاة تقام في رجب على ما قيل
ترجمہ اور مراد ارادہ ہے اس حدیث میں جو روایت کی گئی ہے واللہ اعلم وہ ہے جو سہو کی ضد ہے نہ کہ اختیار دینا اور عتیرہ اور یہ وہ بکری ہوتی تھی جس کو رجب میں ذبح کیا جاتا تھا جیسا کہ کہا گیا ہے۔ تشریح یہ فریق مخالف کی روایت کردہ حدیث کا جواب ہے کہ یہاں ارادہ سے مراد وہ نہیں ہے جو آپ نے سمجھا کہ اختیار دینا مقصود ہے کہ خواہ قربانی کر دیا چھوڑ دو۔ بلکہ ارادہ بمعنی قصد ہے یعنی جو اس واجب کو ادا کرنے کا قصد رکھتا ہے تو اس کو یہ کرنا چاہئے کہ بال وغیرہ نہ کانے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے من اراد الصلاة فليتوضا، ومن اراد الجمعة فليغتسل بل اللفظ ارادہ سے یہ سنیت پر استدلال ہے درست نہیں ہے۔
رہا عتیرہ پر قیاس کرنا تو یہ بھی خلاف اصول ہے کیونکہ یہ منسوخ ہے اور منسوخ پر حکم مطلوب کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ تنبیہ عتیرہ کی تعریف میں اقوال مختلفہ ہیں، ایک وہ جو مذکورہ ہے اور دوسرے یہ اونٹنی کا جو پہلا بچہ ہوتا تھا اس کو ذبح کرتے تھے وغیرہ وغیرہ۔
Answer to the opposing school's hadith: And the meaning of 'irada' in what is narrated—and Allah knows best—is that which is the opposite of forgetfulness, not that it is a choice. And 'Atirah is abrogated, and it is a sheep that is slaughtered in Rajab, as is said. Translation: And the meaning of 'irada' in this hadith that is narrated—and Allah knows best—is that which is the opposite of forgetfulness, not giving a choice. And 'Atirah is that she-goat which used to be slaughtered in Rajab, as is said. Explanation: This is an answer to the hadith narrated by the opposing school: that here the meaning of 'irada' is not what you understood, that giving a choice is intended, that one may either perform the sacrifice or leave it. Rather, 'irada' means intention (qasd), that is, the one who intends to perform this wajib should not cut his hair etc. And this is like the statement: 'Whoever intends to pray, let him perform wudu; whoever intends to attend Friday prayer, let him perform ghusl.' Rather, using the word 'irada' to deduce that it is sunnah is not correct. As for making an analogy to 'Atirah, that is also against principles because it is abrogated, and the desired ruling cannot be analogized to an abrogated one. Note: There are different opinions regarding the definition of 'Atirah: one is what was mentioned, and another is that it was the first offspring of a she-camel which they used to slaughter, etc.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The opposing school (likely Shafi'i) used a hadith containing the word 'irada' (intention/choice) to argue that the prohibition on cutting hair and nails for one intending sacrifice is not obligatory but merely recommended. The Hanafi commentator clarifies that 'irada' here means purpose or resolve (the opposite of forgetfulness), not giving a choice. He supports this by citing similar usages in commands related to prayer and Friday bath. He then refutes the opposing school's analogy to 'Atirah (a pre-Islamic practice) by stating that 'Atirah is abrogated, and analogy cannot be based on an abrogated ruling. Finally, he notes different definitions of 'Atirah among scholars.

Key Terms
الارادة (al-irada): In this context, it means resolve and firm intention (qasd), not choice or permission.
العتيرة (al-'atirah): A sheep or goat slaughtered in Rajab as a pre-Islamic practice; abrogated in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, what does 'irada' mean in the hadith about one intending sacrifice?
A) A choice to sacrifice or not
B) Resolve and intention (qasd), opposite of forgetfulness
C) A mere recommendation
D) An abrogated ruling

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that 'irada' means firm intention (qasd), making it wajib to refrain from cutting hair before sacrifice; 'Atirah is abrogated and cannot be used for analogy.

Five Conditions for Sacrifice (Udhiyah) to Be Obligatory
Enumeration of five conditions for sacrifice to be obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for Udhiyah to be wajib and distinguish the wealth condition from that of zakat.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is wajib on the free, Muslim, resident, wealthy person during the days of sacrifice; wealth threshold equals sadaqat al-fitr, not zakat.

This lesson unpacks the five conditions that make the annual sacrifice (Udhiyah) obligatory in the Hanafi school. Based on al-Quduri's matn and its commentary, we will explore why each condition is required and how the wealth condition differs from zakat. By the end, you will be able to apply these conditions to real cases and understand the rationale behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that the act is Udhiyah (sacrifice) and the ruling is wajib (obligatory) for those who meet the conditions.
Hanafi: wajib; Shafi'i: sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
List the five conditions
Extract the five conditions from the text: freedom, Islam, residency, wealth, and time (days of sacrifice).
Each condition has a specific rationale.
3
Examine the rationale for each condition
For each condition, read the commentator's explanation: freedom requires ownership; Islam because it is worship; residency because travel exempts; wealth to have capacity; time because sacrifice is specific to those days.
Focus on the wealth condition: it is like sadaqat al-fitr, not like zakat.
4
Distinguish wealth for sacrifice from wealth for zakat
Note that sacrifice requires possession of nisab beyond essential needs, but the wealth need not be productive nor one year old. Contrast with zakat, which requires productive wealth and the passage of a year.
Example: surplus houses or oxen used for work are essential needs and not counted.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a detailed scenario (e.g., a free Muslim resident with nisab from non-productive assets), determine if sacrifice is wajib.
Check each condition in order.

پانچویں شرط وقت قربانی کا ہونا یعنی ایام نحر کا ہونا کیونکہ قربانی انہی ایام کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یہاں اتنی مالداری شرط ہے جتنی صدقہ فطر میں یعنی مقدار نصاب مال ہوتا تو شرط ہے مگر اس کا نامی ہونا اور اس پر سال گزرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
اگر کسی کے پاس دو مکان ہیں اور ایک میں وہ رہتا ہے اور دوسرا اس کی ضرورت سے زائد ہے اور اس کی قیمت بقد رنصاب ہے تو اس پر اس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ تو واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ مال نامی نہیں ہے البتہ قربانی اور صدقہ فطر واجب ہو گا۔ بالفاظ دیگر صدقہ فطر اور قربانی کا وجوب نیز حج کا وجوب قدرت ممکنہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور زکوۃ وغیرہ کا وجوب قدرت میسرہ کی وجہ سے ہے۔
تنبیہ کاشتکار کے پاس دو بیل ہیں جن سے وہ ہل چلاتا ہے اگر چہ بل پورے سال نہیں چلتا ہے بلکہ مخصوص موسم میں چلتا ہے اس کے باوجود بھی یہ بیل حوائج اصلیہ میں داخل ہوں گے اور اس کی وجہ سے اس پر قربانی واجب نہ ہوگی، والناس عنه غافلون
And the obligation is specifically tied to freedom because it is a financial duty that is only fulfilled through ownership, and the owner is the free person. And it is tied to Islam because it is an act of worship. And to residency due to what we explained. And to wealth due to the hadith we narrated about the condition of capacity. Its measure is that which obligates sadaqat al-fitr, and it has passed in the book of fasting. And the time is the day of sacrifice because it is specific to it, and we will soon mention its measure, Allah willing. Translation: And the obligation is specific to freedom because sacrifice is a financial duty that is not fulfilled except by ownership, and the owner is the free person. And the obligation is specific to Islam because sacrifice is an act of worship. And the obligation is specific to residency due to the proof we have mentioned. And the obligation is specific to wealth due to the hadith we narrated, meaning the condition of capacity, and the amount is that which obligates sadaqat al-fitr, and it has been discussed in the book of fasting (i.e., chapter of sadaqat al-fitr). And the obligation is specific to the time, and that is the day of sacrifice because sacrifice is specific to it, and we will soon mention the measure of the time, Allah willing. Explanation: Detail of the second and third discussions, an explanation of the conditions that al-Quduri mentioned. First condition: being free, because sacrifice requires ownership, and a slave does not have the capacity to be an owner; rather he is owned, so ownership is specific to the free. Second condition: being Muslim, because sacrifice is an act of worship, and a disbeliever is not qualified to perform acts of worship. Third condition: being resident, its proof was mentioned previously, i.e., 'Verily the performance is specific to a cause that is difficult...' etc. Fourth condition: being wealthy, which is understood from the hadith mentioned previously, 'Whoever finds capacity...' etc. Fifth condition: the time of sacrifice, i.e., the days of sacrifice, because sacrifice is specific to these days. Here, the wealth is the same condition as in sadaqat al-fitr, i.e., having wealth of nisab amount is a condition, but it does not require it to be productive nor one year to pass. If someone has two houses, one he lives in and the other is surplus to his need, and its value equals the nisab, then zakat is not obligatory because the wealth is not productive, but sacrifice and sadaqat al-fitr become wajib. In other words, the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr and sacrifice, and also hajj, is due to potential ability (qudrat mumkinah), while the obligation of zakat etc. is due to actual ability (qudrat muyassarah). Note: If a farmer has two oxen with which he plows, even if the oxen do not work the whole year but only in a specific season, these oxen are still considered essential needs (hawa'ij asliyyah), so due to them, sacrifice is not wajib, and people are heedless of this.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating five conditions for the obligation of Udhiyah (sacrifice) as stated by al-Quduri. The commentator expands each condition: (1) Freedom: only free persons can own property, and sacrifice requires ownership. (2) Islam: sacrifice is an act of worship, so it is only valid from a Muslim. (3) Residency (being muqim): the traveler is exempt, as per earlier discussion. (4) Wealth: the same threshold as sadaqat al-fitr (nisab), but unlike zakat, the wealth need not be productive nor pass one year. (5) Time: the days of sacrifice (10-12 Dhul-Hijjah). The commentator clarifies that wealth for sacrifice is like sadaqat al-fitr: if one possesses nisab beyond essential needs, sacrifice is wajib even if the wealth is not growing. This is contrasted with zakat, which requires productive wealth. A farmer's oxen are considered essential needs, so they do not count toward the nisab for sacrifice.

Key Terms
الحرية (al-hurriyyah): Freedom: being a free person, not a slave, because sacrifice requires ownership.
اليسار (al-yasar): Wealth or capacity: possessing wealth of nisab amount beyond essential needs, same threshold as sadaqat al-fitr.
الاقامة (al-iqamah): Residency: being a resident (muqim), not a traveler (musafir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi conditions, what is the wealth threshold for sacrifice to be wajib?
A) The same as zakat: productive nisab with one year passing
B) The same as sadaqat al-fitr: possessing nisab beyond essential needs without requiring it to be productive
C) Any amount of wealth regardless of need
D) Only cash and trade goods

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah is wajib upon a free, Muslim, resident who possesses nisab (like sadaqat al-fitr) during the days of sacrifice; the wealth need not be productive.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Sacrifice for the Minor Child
Intra-Hanafi dispute relying on qiyas and principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations regarding sacrifice (udhiyah) for a minor child, explain why the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position holds it is not wajib, and apply the principle of qurbah mahdah.

Core Idea
Sacrifice for a minor child is not wajib according to the authoritative Hanafi narration, because it is a pure worship not analogized to sadaqat al-fitr.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute: is a father required to sacrifice on behalf of his minor child? Two narrations from Abu Hanifa exist. The later, more widely transmitted position (zahir al-riwayah) states it is not wajib, while a rare narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad deems it obligatory by analogy to sadaqat al-fitr. Understanding why the school prefers the non-obligation position requires grasping the distinction between financial obligations and pure acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) a narration of Hasan making sacrifice wajib for the minor child by analogy to sadaqat al-fitr; (2) the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) making it not wajib.
These are both attributed to Abu Hanifa, but one is from the nawadir and the other from the main corpus.
2
Examine the proof for the wajib position
The wajib position uses qiyas: just as sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for the child, so is sacrifice, because the child is considered like part of the father's self.
This is a qiyas jaliy argument.
3
Examine the proof for the non-wajib position
The non-wajib position distinguishes sacrifice from sadaqat al-fitr. The cause for sadaqat al-fitr is maintenance and guardianship, which exist for the minor. But sacrifice is a pure worship (qurbah mahdah), and the principle is that worship is not obligatory on behalf of another.
This is a distinction based on differing illas.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is given preference because it is from the well-known transmitted corpus, and the principle of qurbah mahdah is a stronger usul than the analogy to sadaqat al-fitr.
The mufta bihi position is that sacrifice is not wajib for the minor child.
5
Apply the principle to the slave case
The passage illustrates the principle further: sacrifice is not wajib for a slave either, even though sadaqat al-fitr is wajib. This reinforces that the distinction is based on the nature of the act (pure worship vs. financial obligation).
This confirms that the ruling is not limited to children but applies to any dependent where worship is not tied to maintenance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتجب عن نفسه لانه اصل فى الوجوب عليه على ما بيناه وعن ولده الصغير لانه في معنى نفسه فیلحق به كما في صدقة الفطر وهذه رواية الحسن عن ابي حنيفة رحمهما الله وروى عنه انه لا يجب عن ولده وهو ظاهر الرواية بخلاف صدقة الفطر لان السبب هناك برأس يمونه ويلي عليه وهما موجودان فى الصغير وهذه قربة محضة والاصل فى القرب ان لا تجب على الغير بسبب الغير ولهذا لا تجب عن عبده وان كان يجب عنه صدقة الفطر
ترجمہ اور قربانی واجب ہے اپنی طرف سے اس لئے کہ انسان اصل ہے اپنے اوپر وجوب کے سلسلہ میں اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں (باب صدقہ الفطر میں ) اور قربانی واجب ہے اپنے چھوٹے بچہ کی طرف سے اس لئے کہ چھوٹا بچہ آدمی کے نفس کے درجہ میں ہے تو وہ بچہ اس کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا جیسے صدقہ فطر میں اور یہ ابو حنیفہ سے حسن کی روایت ہے اور مروی ہے ابو حنیفہ سے کہ قربانی واجب نہیں ہے اپنے بچہ کی طرف سے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے بخلاف صدقہ فطر کے اس لئے کہ سبب وہاں ایسی راس (ذات) ہے جس کے وہ نفقہ کا ذمہ دار ہے اور اس پر ولایت رکھتا ہو اور یہ دونوں باتیں (مونت و ولایت) موجود ہیں صغیر میں اور یہ (قربانی) قربت محض ہے اور اصل قرب میں یہ ہے کہ دوسرے کی طرف سے وجوب نہ ہو، اس لئے غلام کی طرف سے قربانی واجب نہیں اگرچہ صدقہ فطر واجب ہے۔
And sacrifice is wajib for oneself because a person is the primary subject of obligation upon himself, as we explained. And it is wajib for his minor child because the minor child is in the position of his self, so it is attached to him, as in sadaqat al-fitr. This is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on them both. And it is narrated from him that it is not wajib for his child, and that is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), unlike sadaqat al-fitr, because the cause there is a dependent person for whom he is responsible for maintenance and over whom he has guardianship, and both exist in the minor. And this (sacrifice) is a pure act of worship, and the principle regarding acts of worship is that they do not become obligatory upon another due to another. For this reason, it is not wajib for his slave, although sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for him. Translation: And sacrifice is wajib for oneself because a person is the origin in the matter of obligation upon himself, according to the detail we have explained (in the chapter of sadaqat al-fitr). And sacrifice is wajib for one's minor child because the minor child is in the position of the person's self, so the child is attached to him, as in sadaqat al-fitr. This is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that sacrifice is not wajib for his child, and that is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), unlike sadaqat al-fitr, because the cause there is a person (ra's) for whom he is responsible for maintenance and over whom he has guardianship, and both these things (maintenance and guardianship) exist in the minor. And this (sacrifice) is a pure act of worship, and the principle regarding acts of worship is that it should not be obligatory upon one due to another. For this reason, it is not wajib for his slave, although sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for him.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether sacrifice is wajib for one's minor child. Two narrations from Abu Hanifa are presented: (1) The narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad (considered a rare narration) states that sacrifice is wajib for the minor child by analogy to sadaqat al-fitr, because the child is like part of oneself. (2) The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) states that sacrifice is NOT wajib for the minor child, unlike sadaqat al-fitr, because the cause for sadaqat al-fitr is that the person is a dependent for whom the father is responsible (maintenance and guardianship). For sacrifice, it is a pure act of worship, and the principle is that worship is not obligatory on behalf of someone else. For this reason, sacrifice is not wajib for a slave either, even though sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for a slave. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the apparent narration.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted narrations from the early Hanafi imams (especially the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani). Here it refers to the position that sacrifice is not wajib for the minor child.
قربة محضة (qurbah mahdah): A pure act of worship, with no worldly benefit or exchange; the principle is that it cannot be obligatory on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), is sacrifice wajib for one's minor child?
A) Yes, by analogy to sadaqat al-fitr
B) No, because it is a pure act of worship and the principle is that worship is not obligatory on behalf of another
C) Yes, only if the child owns property
D) No, the sacrifice is only for the father himself

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that sacrifice is not wajib for a minor child because it is a pure act of worship, distinguished from the financial obligation of sadaqat al-fitr.

Five Conditions for the Obligation of Udhiyah
Enumerates the five conditions for udhiyah to be wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the five conditions for udhiyah to be wajib and EXPLAIN how the wealth condition differs from zakat.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is wajib upon every free, Muslim, resident who possesses nisab of surplus wealth on the days of sacrifice.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling from Al-Hidayah that sets out who must offer the udhiyah sacrifice. These five conditions define the obligation precisely, distinguishing it from other obligatory acts such as zakat. The text also includes a crucial tanbih about agricultural tools, a detail often overlooked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
List them from the text: free, Muslim, resident, wealthy (nisab), and time of sacrifice.
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
For each, the text gives a brief reason: ownership (free), capacity for worship (Muslim), hardship (resident), hadith proof (wealthy), specificity of days (time).
3
Compare the wealth condition to zakat
Note the differences: nisab same but no growth requirement nor year, and the basis is qudrat mumkinah not muyassarah.
4
Apply the tanbih (oxen example)
Understand that plough oxen are basic necessities even if seasonal, so they do not count toward nisab for udhiyah.
5
Test your memory with the five conditions in order
Recite: Free, Muslim, Resident, Wealthy, Time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پہلی شرط آزاد ہونا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قربانی کے لئے ملکیت چاہئیے اور غلام میں مالک ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں بلکہ وہ ملوک ہے یعنی مالک ہونا صرف آزاد کے لئے مخصوص ہے۔ دوسری شرط مسلمان ہونا اس لئے کہ قربانی قربت ہے اور کا فرقربات کی ادائیگی کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ تیسری شرط مقیم ہونا جس کی دلیل ماقبل میں بیان کی جاچکی ہے یعنی غیر ان الاداء يختص باسبا ب يشق .... الخ ۔ چوتھی شرط مالدار ہونا جو ماقبل میں ذکر کردہ حدیث سے مفہوم ہے من وجد سعة .... الخ پانچویں شرط وقت قربانی کا ہونا یعنی ایام نحر کا ہونا کیونکہ قربانی انہی ایام کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یہاں اتنی مالداری شرط ہے جتنی صدقہ فطر میں یعنی مقدار نصاب مال ہوتو شرط ہے مگر اس کا نامی ہونا اور اس پر سال گزرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اگر کسی کے پاس دو مکان ہیں اور ایک میں وہ رہتا ہے اور دوسرا اس کی ضرورت سے زائد ہے اور اس کی قیمت بقد رنصاب ہے تو اس پر اس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ تو واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ مال نامی نہیں ہے البتہ قربانی اور صدقہ فطر واجب ہو گا۔ بالفاظ دیگر صدقہ فطر اور قربانی کا وجوب نیز حج کا وجوب قدرت ممکنہ کی وجہ سے ہے اور زکوۃ وغیرہ کا وجوب قدرت میسرہ کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تنبیہ کاشتکار کے پاس دو بیل ہیں جن سے وہ ہل چلاتا ہے اگر چہ بل پورے سال نہیں چلتا ہے بلکہ مخصوص موسم میں چلتا ہے اس کے باوجود بھی یہ بیل حوائج اصلیہ میں داخل ہوں گے اور اس کی وجہ سے اس پر قربانی واجب نہ ہوگی، والناس عنه غافلون
First condition: being free. The reason is that sacrifice requires ownership, and a slave has no capacity for ownership; rather he is owned – ownership is specific to the free person. Second condition: being Muslim, because sacrifice is an act of worship and a disbeliever is not qualified to perform acts of worship. Third condition: being a resident, the proof for which was mentioned earlier, i.e., 'the performance is specific to a person who has the capacity for hardship...' etc. Fourth condition: being wealthy, which is understood from the hadith mentioned earlier: 'whoever finds capacity...' etc. Fifth condition: that the time of sacrifice be present, i.e., the days of sacrifice, because sacrifice is specific to these days. Here, the required wealth is the same as in sadaqat al-fitr, i.e., the amount of nisab is a condition, but for it to be growing (nami) and for a year to pass over it is not necessary. If someone has two houses, one in which he lives and the other is surplus to his need, and its value is to the extent of nisab, then due to it zakat is not wajib upon him because the wealth is not growing; however, udhiyah and sadaqat al-fitr become wajib. In other words, the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah, as well as Hajj, is due to capacity based on possibility (qudrat mumkinah), while the obligation of zakat etc. is due to capacity based on availability (qudrat muyassarah). Warning: A farmer possesses two oxen with which he ploughs; even if the oxen do not work the whole year but only in a specific season, despite this, these oxen are included among basic necessities, and due to them udhiyah is not wajib upon him. And people are heedless of this.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the five conditions for the obligation of udhiyah in the Hanafi school. The author begins with freedom: a slave cannot own property and thus cannot perform the act of ownership required for sacrifice. Second, Islam: the disbeliever's acts of worship are not valid. Third, residence: the traveler is not obligated because the days of sacrifice may not be valid for him. Fourth, wealth: the minimum is nisab (as in sadaqat al-fitr), but unlike zakat, the wealth need not be growing (nami) nor must a year pass. The example of two houses illustrates that surplus property triggers the obligation of udhiyah and sadaqat al-fitr, but not zakat, because the latter requires growing wealth. The reasoning is that udhiyah and sadaqat al-fitr depend on qudrat mumkinah (feasible capacity) while zakat depends on qudrat muyassarah (readily available capacity). Finally, a tanbih: a farmer's plough oxen are considered basic necessities (hawa'ij asliyyah) even if used only seasonally, so they do not make udhiyah obligatory. This subtle point is often overlooked.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers obligation, here the same as for sadaqat al-fitr.
حوائج اصلیہ (hawa'ij asliyyah): Basic necessities of life such as residential houses, work animals, and tools essential for livelihood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of udhiyah?
A) Being free
B) Being a Muslim
C) The wealth being nami (growing)
D) Being a resident

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah becomes obligatory when five conditions are all met: free, Muslim, resident, nisab of surplus wealth, and the days of sacrifice.

Udhiyah for the Minor Child: Two Hanafi Riwāyāt
Presents two Hanafi narrations on whether udhiyah is wajib for one's minor child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi narrations on udhiyah for the minor child and apply the principle that pure devotions (qurbah mahdah) are not obligatory on behalf of others.

Core Idea
Udhiyah for a minor child is not wajib in the relied-upon narration because it is a pure devotion.

This passage presents a fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the father must sacrifice for his minor child. The author contrasts two riwāyāt from Imam Abu Hanifa, each with its own dalīl. Understanding why the relied-upon view (zāhir al-riwāyah) differs from the narration of Hasan unlocks a key principle about the nature of pure devotions versus devotions with a worldly aspect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Narrations
Locate the two positions attributed to Abu Hanifa: one from Hasan ibn Ziyad (udhiyah is wajib for the child) and the other from zahir al-riwayah (it is not wajib).
The text explicitly contrasts them using 'hadhihi riwayah al-Hasan' and 'wa huwa zahir al-riwayah'.
2
State the Legal Principle for Each
For Hasan's view, the child is 'fi ma'na nafsih' (in the meaning of himself), so it attaches like sadaqat al-fitr. For the zahir al-riwayah, udhiyah is a pure devotion (qurbah mahdah), and the principle is that pure devotions are not obligatory on behalf of another.
3
Examine the Cause for Sadaqat al-Fitr
Sadaqat al-fitr is based on maintenance (mu'nah) and guardianship (wilayah), both present in the child and the slave. Udhiyah lacks these causes.
The text says 'al-sabab hunāka bira's yamu'nuhu wa yali 'alayh'.
4
Apply the Qurbah Mahdah Rule
The general rule: pure devotions are not obligatory on behalf of another due to another. Therefore, udhiyah is not wajib for the child or slave.
This is the decisive principle that distinguishes udhiyah from sadaqat al-fitr.
5
Determine the Muftā Bihī
The text declares the zahir al-riwayah as the relied-upon position. The narration of Hasan is a minority view (nawadir) and not followed in practice.
The author's phrase 'wa huwa zahir al-riwayah' indicates tarjih.

And it is obligatory for himself because he is the basis in obligation upon him as we have explained. And it is obligatory for his young child because the child is in the meaning of himself, so it attaches to him as in sadaqat al-fitr. This is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on both). And it is narrated from him that it is not obligatory for his child, and this is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), contrary to sadaqat al-fitr. The reason there is that the cause is a head for whom he provides maintenance and over whom he has guardianship, and both exist in the minor. And this (udhiyah) is a pure devotion, and the principle in devotions is that they are not obligatory on behalf of another due to another. For this reason, it is not obligatory for his slave, even though it is obligatory for sadaqat al-fitr. Here, there are two riwayat from Abu Hanifa: one is the narration of Hasan which is mentioned, and the other is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and it is that udhiyah is not obligatory for the child. According to this narration, there is a difference between sadaqat al-fitr and udhiyah: the cause of obligation in sadaqat al-fitr is maintenance and guardianship, i.e., it is obligatory for every person for whom he is responsible for maintenance and over whom he has guardianship. Both exist in the child, and the same applies to the slave, so sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory for them. As for the matter of udhiyah, it is a pure devotion, and the rule of devotions is that they are not obligatory for someone due to another. This entire discussion is when the child has no wealth. If he has wealth, then its detail is what is coming now. He says:
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether udhiyah is obligatory for one's minor child. The author first states the general rule: udhiyah is wajib for oneself. Then, he presents two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The first, transmitted by Hasan b. Ziyad, holds that udhiyah is also wajib for a minor child, analogizing to sadaqat al-fitr, where the child is considered like the father's own self. The second, which is the zahir al-riwayah (the relied-upon narration), states that udhiyah is not wajib for the child, unlike sadaqat al-fitr. The reasoning: sadaqat al-fitr is obligatory because the cause (sabab) is the person for whom one provides maintenance (mu'nah) and has guardianship (wilayah). Both are present in the child and the slave. But udhiyah is a pure devotion (qurbah mahdah), and the principle for devotions is that they are not obligatory on behalf of another due to another. Therefore, even though sadaqat al-fitr is wajib for the slave, udhiyah is not. The commentary then clarifies that this applies when the child has no wealth. If the child has wealth, the ruling differs and will be explained next.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The established and widely transmitted narration from Abu Hanifa through his students, considered the primary source of the madhhab.
قربت محضہ (qurbah mahdah): A pure act of worship that has no worldly aspect, unlike sadaqat al-fitr which also provides maintenance.
مونت و ولایت (mu'nah wa wilayah): Maintenance (providing for expenses) and guardianship (legal authority), the dual cause for obligation of sadaqat al-fitr on behalf of dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah of Abu Hanifa, is udhiyah obligatory for a person's minor child if the child has no wealth?
A) Yes, it is wajib like sadaqat al-fitr.
B) No, it is not wajib because udhiyah is a pure devotion.
C) Yes, it is wajib but only if the father intends it.
D) No, it is not wajib because the child is not Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that udhiyah is not wajib for a minor child because it is a pure devotion, unlike sadaqat al-fitr which is based on maintenance and guardianship.

Udhiyah from a Minor's Wealth: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Presents disagreement on whether the father may sacrifice from the minor's own wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on using a minor's wealth for udhiyah and explain the reasoning behind the asahh (most correct) view.

Core Idea
Fathers may sacrifice from a minor's wealth, but only if the minor eats some and the rest is invested for his benefit.

When a minor child possesses wealth, should the father perform the udhiyah (sacrifice) using the child's own money or his own? This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute that also aligns with al-Shafi'i. The resolution balances the obligation of udhiyah with the minor's financial interests, providing a nuanced ruling that you can apply today.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the act (udhiyah for a minor) and the central question: from whose wealth should it be performed?
The act of udhiyah itself is wajib upon the father for himself, but the dispute is about performing it on behalf of a child.
2
Identify the Two Positions
List the positions: (1) Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) – from minor's wealth; (2) Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i – from the father's own wealth.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf that overlaps with Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the Opposing Dalil
The opposing view argues that the devotion (qurbah) is fulfilled by the slaughter; the subsequent charity of meat is supererogatory (tatwawwu') and cannot be spent from a minor's wealth. Also, the minor cannot consume all the meat.
This is a talil (reason-based) argument – no explicit scriptural text cited.
4
Examine the Asahh View and Its Condition
The asahh (most correct) view – from Shaykhayn – permits using the minor's wealth but imposes a condition: the minor must eat as much as possible from the meat, and the remaining proceeds must be used to purchase a lasting benefit for the minor (e.g., a durable asset).
This condition safeguards the minor's wealth while allowing the devotion.
5
Compare with Sadaqat al-Fitr
The text notes that the dispute is analogous to the disagreement on paying sadaqat al-fitr from a minor's wealth. This parallel helps understand the pattern.
The same split among the imams applies to both obligations.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان للصغير مال يضحى عنه ابوه او وصيه من ماله عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف رحمهما الله وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي رحمهم الله يضحى من مال نفسه لامن مال الصغير فالخلاف في هذا كالخلاف في صدقة الفطر وقيل لا يجوز التضحية من مال الصغير فى قولهم لان القربة تنادى بالاراقة والصدقة بعدها تطوع فلا يجوز ذلك من مال الصغير ولا يمكنه ان ياكل كله والاصح ان يضحى من ماله وياكل منه ما امكنه ويبتاع بما بقى ما ينتفع بعينه ترجمہ اور اگر صغیر کے پاس مال ہو تو اس کی جانب سے اس کا باپ یا اس کا وسی بچہ کے مال سے قربانی کرے ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اور فرمایا محمد اور زفر اور شافعی نے کہ اپنے مال سے قربانی کرے نہ کہ بچہ کے مال سے تو اختلاف اس میں صدقہ فطر کے مثل اختلاف کے ہے۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ سب کے قول میں بچہ کے مال سے قربانی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قربت تو خون بہانے سے ادا ہو جاتی ہے اور اس کے بعد صدقہ ایک تطوع ہے پس یہ تطوع جائز نہ ہوگا بچہ کے مال سے اور ممکن نہیں ہے بچہ کو کہ وہ تمام گوشت کھائے اور اصح یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے مال سے قربانی کی جائے اور اس میں سے بچہ اتنا کھالے جتنا کھانا ممکن ہو۔ اور مابقی سے ایسی چیز خرید کی جائے جس کے عین سے نفع اٹھایا جائے۔ تشریح اور اگر بچہ کے پاس مال ہو تو شیخین کے نزدیک بچہ کے مال سے قربانی کی جائے اور امام محمد اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ اپنے مال سے قربانی کرے نہ کہ بچہ کے مال سے جیسا کہ صدقہ فطر میں اختلاف ہے ایسا ہی یہاں ہے۔ یعنی اگر بچہ کے پاس مال ہے تو شیخین کے نزدیک بچہ کے مال سے صدقہ فطر ادا کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ۔ تو
And if the minor has wealth, then his father or his executor sacrifices on his behalf from his wealth according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on both). And Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) said: He sacrifices from his own wealth, not from the minor's wealth. The dispute here is like the dispute in sadaqat al-fitr. And it was said: It is not permissible to sacrifice from the minor's wealth in their [all] statement, because the devotion is fulfilled by spilling blood, and the charity after it is supererogatory. So this supererogatory act is not permissible from the minor's wealth, and it is not possible for the minor to eat all of it. And the most correct (asahh) is that he sacrifices from his wealth, and the minor eats from it as much as possible, and with the remainder he buys something the benefit of whose essence is enjoyed. And Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i said: He sacrifices from his own wealth, not from the minor's wealth. The dispute here is like the dispute in sadaqat al-fitr. And it was said: It is not permissible to sacrifice from the minor's wealth in all their statements, because the devotion is fulfilled by spilling blood, and the charity after it is supererogatory. So this supererogatory act is not permissible from the minor's wealth, and it is not possible for the minor to eat all of it. And the most correct (asahh) is that he sacrifices from his wealth, and the minor eats from it as much as possible, and with the remainder he buys something the benefit of whose essence is enjoyed. Explanation: And if the minor has wealth, then according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the sacrifice should be from the minor's wealth. Imam Muhammad, Imam Zufar, and Imam Shafi'i say: Sacrifice from one's own wealth, not from the minor's wealth, just as the dispute exists in sadaqat al-fitr. That is, if the minor has wealth, according to the Shaykhayn it is permissible to pay sadaqat al-fitr from the minor's wealth, and according to Imam Muhammad it is not permissible. So...
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when a minor child has wealth. The father may perform udhiyah on behalf of the child or have it done by an executor. The author presents three positions. First, the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the sacrifice should be performed from the minor's own wealth. Second, Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i hold that it should be from the father's own wealth. The reasoning for the latter is that the devotion (qurbah) is accomplished by slaughtering the animal, and the charity of the meat that follows is supererogatory (tatwawwu'). It is not permissible to give supererogatory charity from the minor's wealth, nor can the minor consume all the meat himself. A third view is attributed (in 'qil') that in all these opinions, it is not permissible at all to sacrifice from the minor's wealth. Finally, the text declares the most correct (asahh) opinion: the sacrifice should be from the minor's wealth, with the minor eating as much as possible, and the remainder used to purchase something of lasting benefit for the minor. This nuanced ruling balances the act of worship with the minor's interest.

Key Terms
شیخین (shaykhayn): Refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf together, the two primary authorities of the Hanafi school.
اصح (asahh): The most correct (most sound) opinion according to later Hanafi scholars, given when there is dispute.
تطوع (tatwawwu'): Supererogatory act, here referring to the charity of meat after the obligatory slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct (asahh) view in the text, what should be done with the meat of an udhiyah sacrificed from a minor's wealth?
A) All of it must be given in charity.
B) The minor should eat as much as possible, and the remainder should be used to buy something beneficial.
C) All of it must be given to the father.
D) The meat must be sold and the money saved.

Key Takeaway
The asahh Hanafi view permits using a minor's wealth for udhiyah, but only if the minor eats some meat and the rest is invested for his benefit.

Qurbani from a Minor's Wealth: Authority vs. Soundness
Explains the Hanafi difference on qurbani from a minor's wealth and the mufta bihi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling on qurbani from a minor's wealth and explain why the asahh view is not followed in practice.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows Zahir al-Riwayah not the asahh — authority trumps individual preference.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: whether a father may perform qurbani using the wealth of his minor child. The apparent position from Zahir al-Riwayah is prohibition, but a later sounder view (asahh) permits it with conditions. However, the relied-upon fatwa remains the earlier prohibition. This lesson explores the reasoning behind both positions and the hierarchy that determines which is operative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal context
Recognize that the act is qurbani (sacrificial slaughter) and that the agent is a minor child (saghir) whose wealth is managed by the guardian (father). Determine what ruling the guardian seeks: performing qurbani from the minor's wealth.
2
Understand the two objectives of qurbani
The passage states that qurbani has two aims: araqat al-dam (spilling blood, which is destruction of wealth) and tasadduq (giving meat in charity). Both conflict with the guardian's limited authority over the minor's property: he cannot destroy it nor give it away without the minor's benefit.
This reasoning is the dalil for prohibition.
3
Examine the asahh view's solution
Al-Marghinani presents a more sound (asahh) view: the qurbani is permissible if the child eats what he can, and the remainder is sold for durable goods (e.g., a chest, bed) that the child can use. This avoids outright destruction and charity of the wealth.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and its authority
Despite the asahh view, the passage explicitly states that fatwa is upon Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), which prohibits qurbani from the minor's wealth. The rule is that Zahir al-Riwayah has priority over individual preferences (asahh).
This is a key principle in Hanafi tarjih: authority weight > apparent soundness.
5
Apply the hierarchy to real fatwa
When giving a fatwa, a mufti must follow the mufta bihi (Zahir al-Riwayah) and not the asahh. The guardian cannot perform qurbani from the minor's wealth; if he wishes, he must use his own wealth or wait until the minor is mature.
Practical consequence: the father is not required or allowed to use the child's money for qurbani.

Source Text

یہی اختلاف قربانی کے اندر ہے۔
۲۷۵
مبسوط اور کافی میں مذکور ہے کہ صغیر کے مال سے کسی کے نزدیک قربانی جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ قربانی میں دو مقصد ہیں:
(۱) اراقت دم جس کا مال اتلاف ہے۔
(۲) گوشت کا تصدق، حالانکہ باپ نہ بچہ کے مال کو تلف کرنے کا مالک ہے اور نہ اس کے مال کو صدقہ کیا جاسکتا ہے اور بچہ سارا گوشت کھائے تو یہ ناممکن ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اصح یہ ہے کہ بچہ کے مال سے قربانی کی جائے اور بچہ جتنا گوشت کھا سکے کھالے اور باقی کو ایسی چیز کے بدلہ میں فروخت کر دیا جائے جس کا مین باقی رہے تا کہ بچہ اس سے نفع اٹھاتا ہے جیسے صندوق، چار پائی، ڈول، مشک وغیرہ۔ تنبیہ فتویٰ ظاہر الروایہ پر ہے نہ بچہ کی طرف سے قربانی کرنا باپ پر واجب ہے اور نہ بچہ کے مال سے جائز ہے، والفتویٰ علی ظاہر الروایہ، شامی ص ۲۰۰ ج ۵ فتاوی قاضی خان علی الہندیہ ص ۳۴۴ ج ۳ و المعتمد هوا لأول وفى المواهب انه اصح ما يفتى به، سكب الا نهر ص ۴۳۴ ج ۳
This same difference of opinion exists regarding qurbani. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Kafi that qurbani from the wealth of a minor is not permissible according to anyone, because qurbani has two objectives: (1) spilling blood, which is destruction of wealth, and (2) charity of meat, whereas the father does not own the right to destroy the child's wealth nor can he give charity from it, and if the child eats all the meat, that is impossible. The author of al-Hidayah says that the sounder view (asahh) is that qurbani should be performed from the child's wealth, and the child should eat as much meat as he can, and the remainder should be sold in exchange for something durable so that the child benefits from it, like a chest, bed, bucket, waterskin, etc. Note: The fatwa is based on Zahir al-Riwayah: it is neither obligatory for the father to perform qurbani on behalf of the child, nor is it permissible from the child's wealth. And the fatwa is upon Zahir al-Riwayah. (Shami vol.5 p.200, Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Hindiyya vol.3 p.344, and al-Mu'tamad is the first, and in al-Mawahib it is said that it is the soundest view to give fatwa upon. Sakh al-Nahr vol.3 p.434)
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of qurbani (sacrificial animal) from the wealth of a minor child who has not reached puberty. The Hanafi school has a difference of opinion on this matter. The initial ruling presented from al-Mabsut and al-Kafi is that it is not permissible at all, because qurbani involves two purposes: (1) the shedding of blood (araqat al-dam), which is a form of destroying wealth (itlaf al-mal), and (2) giving the meat in charity (tasadduq). Since a father does not have the right to destroy his child's wealth arbitrarily, nor can he give the child's wealth in charity (as charity requires ownership and intention), and if the child were to eat all the meat (which is unlikely), it would defeat the purpose. Therefore, it is not allowed. However, the author of al-Hidayah (Al-Marghinani) states that the more correct view (asahh) is that qurbani is permissible from the child's wealth, but with conditions: the child is to eat as much meat as he can, and the remainder is to be sold in exchange for something durable (like a chest, bed, bucket, waterskin) so that the child retains benefit from it. This solves the issue of destruction and charity. Nevertheless, the passage ends with a clear note (tanbih) that the fatwa (operative ruling) is upon Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad), which states that qurbani from a minor's wealth is not permissible, nor is it obligatory for the father to perform qurbani on behalf of the child. The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is the first (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is considered the soundest view for fatwa. This shows the hierarchy in Hanafi fiqh: the asahh (sounder) is not necessarily the mufta bihi; the authority weight of Zahir al-Riwayah overrides individual preferences.

Key Terms
صغیر (saghir): A minor child who has not reached puberty (bulugh). In this lesson, the subject of the dispute: can qurbani be performed using his wealth?
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. In this passage, they contain the ruling that qurbani from a minor's wealth is not permissible, and fatwa is based on this.
اصح (asahh): The view considered more correct by the commentator (al-Marghinani) based on evidence and reasoning. Here, it permits qurbani with conditions, but it is not the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) regarding qurbani from a minor's wealth?
A) It is permissible unconditionally.
B) It is not permissible; fatwa is on Zahir al-Riwayah.
C) It is obligatory for the father to do it.
D) It is permissible only if the minor eats all the meat.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi ruling on qurbani from a minor's wealth is that it is not permissible, despite a sounder view allowing it, because fatwa follows Zahir al-Riwayah's authority.

Number of Persons per Qurbani Animal: Qiyas Overridden by Athar
Ruling with proof: states the ruling and the usul reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing a qurbani animal and explain why the hadith of Jabir overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
A cow or camel can be shared by seven, but a sheep is only for one — because the hadith overrides qiyas only for large animals.

This passage from al-Quduri lays down a foundational ruling about qurbani sharing. It introduces a classic Hanafi usul principle: when a clear tradition (athar) contradicts analogical reasoning (qiyas), the tradition prevails — but only where the tradition exists. The ruling hinges on the presence or absence of a specific textual proof (nass). Let us walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling per animal type
State the rule: sheep are for one person only; cow and camel can be shared by up to seven persons.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Recognise that by qiyas, even a large animal should be for one person because the act of worship (araqat al-dam) is a single act.
The qiyas is based on the unity of the ritual act.
3
Locate the overriding evidence (athar)
Identify the hadith of Jabir (ra) in which the Prophet (saw) sacrificed a cow and a camel for seven persons each.
This is an explicit, clear-text proof (nass) for large animals.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Understand that the hadith (athar) specifies (takhsis) the general qiyas, so the qiyas is abandoned for large animals.
The principle: al-athar yuqaddam 'ala al-qiyas.
5
Determine the ruling for sheep
Since no such hadith exists for sheep, the original qiyas remains, confining a sheep to one person.
No nass → qiyas stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويذبح عـن كـل واحد منهم شاة اويذبح بقرة أو بدنة عن سبعة والقياس ان لا تجوز الا عن واحد لان الاراقة واحدة وهى القربة الا انا تركناه بالاثر وهو ماروى عن جابر رضى الله عنه انه قال نحرنا مع رسول الله عليه السلام البقرة عن سبعة والبدنة عن سبعة ولا نص في الشاة فبقى على اصل القياس
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور آدمی ذبح کرے ان میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے (یعنی اپنی اور اپنی اولاد میں سے ہر ایک کی) ایک بکری یا ذبح کرے ایک گائے یا ایک اونٹ سات کی طرف سے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو (گائے اور اونٹ) مگر ایک کی جانب سے اس لئے کہ اراقت (خون بہانا) ایک ہے مگر ہم نے اثر کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا ہے اور اثر وہ ہے جو جابر سے مروی ہے کہ انہوں نے کہا کہ ہم نے قربان کیا گائے کو سات آدمیوں کی طرف سے اور اونٹ کو سات کی طرف سے اور بکری کے سلسلہ میں کوئی نص نہیں تو بکری اصل قیاس پر باقی رہی۔ تشریح بکری کی قربانی فقط ایک کی طرف سے ہو سکتی ہے اور بڑے جانوروں کی جیسے گائے اونٹ وغیرہ کی سات کی طرف سے ہوسکتی ہے۔ اگر چہ قیاس کا تقاضہ بڑے جانور میں بھی یہ تھا کہ صرف ایک کی طرف سے ہو کیوں کہ وہ بھی نفس واحد ہے اور اراقت دم بھی دونوں میں متحد ہے متعدد نہیں اور اراقت دم ہی قربت ہے۔ مگر ہم نے حدیث جابر کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ دیا حدیث وہ ہے جو مذکور ہے اور حدیث صرف بڑے جانوروں کے سلسلے میں ہے لہذا بکری قیاس کے مطابق رہی، کیوں کہ اس کے بارے میں کوئی نص نہیں ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And a man should slaughter for each one of them (i.e., for himself and each of his children) one sheep, or slaughter a cow or a camel for seven. And the qiyas (analogy) is that it is not permissible except for one, because the spilling of blood (araqah) is one, and it is the act of worship. However, we have abandoned the qiyas due to the athar (tradition), which is what is narrated from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) the cow for seven and the camel for seven, and there is no nass (text) regarding the sheep, so it remains on the original qiyas. Translation: Al-Quduri said: A man should slaughter for each one of them (i.e., himself and his children) one sheep, or slaughter one cow or one camel for seven. And the qiyas is that it is not permissible (for cow/camel) except for one, because the spilling of blood (araqat) is one. But we have abandoned the qiyas due to the athar, which is narrated from Jabir that he said: We sacrificed the cow for seven people and the camel for seven people, and there is no nass regarding the sheep, so the sheep remains on the original qiyas. Explanation: The qurbani of a sheep can only be for one person, and big animals like cow, camel, etc., can be for seven. Although qiyas would require that a big animal also be for only one, because it is a single animal and the spilling of blood is one act, not multiple, and the spilling of blood is the act of worship. But we have abandoned the qiyas due to the hadith of Jabir which is mentioned, and the hadith is only regarding big animals, so the sheep remains according to qiyas because there is no nass about it.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage states the basic ruling on the number of persons that can share in a qurbani animal. According to the matn (al-Quduri), a person should slaughter one sheep for each individual (himself and his children) or slaughter a cow or camel for seven persons. The passage then explains the legal reasoning (qiyas) and the exception. By qiyas, a big animal like a cow or camel should only suffice for one person because the act of worship is the spilling of blood, which is a single act regardless of the animal's size. However, this qiyas is overridden by a specific tradition (athar) from the hadith of Jabir (ra) that the Prophet (saw) allowed sacrificing a cow or camel for seven persons. No such hadith exists for sheep, so the sheep remains on the original qiyas (one sheep per person). Thus, the ruling is: sheep = one person; cow/camel = up to seven persons. This is a clear example of takhsis al-qiyas bi al-athar (specifying analogy by tradition).

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: Here, the qiyas is that since the act of worship (araqat al-dam) is one, a single animal should only be for one person.
اثر (athar): A tradition or narration from the Companions or the Prophet (saw). In this context, it refers to the hadith of Jabir.
نص (nass): A clear textual evidence (from Quran or Sunnah). Here, there is no nass regarding sheep, so qiyas remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many persons can a cow be sacrificed for?
A) One person only
B) Up to seven persons
C) Up to ten persons
D) Only for the owner and his family

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a sheep is for one person, while cow and camel can be shared by up to seven persons, based on the hadith of Jabir overriding qiyas.

Sharing a Big Animal for Qurbani: Number and Share Requirements
Rules for sharing big animals among fewer or more than seven

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing a cow or camel for qurbani, identify the condition that each share must be at least one-seventh, and apply the ruling to scenarios with different numbers of participants.

Core Idea
A cow or camel may be shared by up to seven, but if any share is less than one-seventh, the sacrifice is invalid for all.

The Hanafi school allows sharing a large animal (cow or camel) for qurbani among up to seven persons. This lesson expands on that ruling: fewer than seven is even more permissible, but sharing among more than seven is not allowed. Additionally, a critical condition is that every participant's share must be at least one-seventh of the animal; otherwise, the sacrifice is invalid for everyone. We will examine the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is sharing a big animal (cow/camel) for qurbani. The default ruling from the text is that it is permissible (ja'iz) for up to seven persons.
This is based on the hadith of Jabir (RA) that the Prophet (PBUH) allowed seven to share a camel or cow.
2
Apply the principle of qiyas al-awlawi
Since sharing among seven is permissible, sharing among fewer (five, six, three) is even more fitting (bi-darajat ula). This is a fortiori analogy: what holds for a larger number holds more strongly for a smaller number.
This reasoning is explicitly mentioned in the text as 'lammā jāza 'an sab'atin fa-'an man dūnahum awlā'.
3
Recognize the condition regarding share size
Each participant's share must be at least one-seventh of the animal. If any share is less than that, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the attribute of being a devotional act (wasf al-qurbah) is absent for that person.
The condition is not about the number of participants alone; it is about the proportion of the animal each receives.
4
Understand the consequence of violation
If any share falls below one-seventh, the entire sharing arrangement becomes invalid—no one's qurbani is accepted. This is why sharing among eight is automatically invalid (since each share would be 1/8 < 1/7), and even with fewer than seven, if shares are unevenly divided causing a deficiency, the same rule applies.
The text states: 'wa lā tajūzu 'an thamāniyatin' and 'in kāna naṣību aḥadihim aqalla min al-sab'i lā yajūzu 'an al-kulli'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سات سے کم آدمیوں کی طرف سے بڑے جانور کی قربانی کا حکم
وتجوز عن خمسة اوستة او ثلثة ذكره محمد فى الاصل لانه لما جاز عن سبعة فعمن دونهم أولى ولا تجوز عن ثمانية اخذا بالقياس فيما لا نص فيه وكذا اذا كان نصيب احدهم اقل من السبع لا يجوز عن الكل لانعدام وصف القربة فى البعض و نبين ه ان شاء تعالی
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے یہ (گائے اور اونٹ) پانچ یا چھ کی طرف سے اس کو محمد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب کہ جائز ہے یہ سات کی طرف سے تو سات سے کم کی طرف سے بدرجہ اولی، اور جائز نہیں ہے آٹھ کی طرف سے قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس کے بارے میں جس کے سلسلہ میں نص نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ ان میں سے ایک کا حصہ ساتویں سے کم ہو تو کل کی طرف سے جائز نہ ہوگی بعض کے اندر وصف قربت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ہم انشاء اللہ اس کو عنقریب بیان کریں گے۔
تشریح بڑے جانور میں سے سات آدمیوں کی شرکت جائز ہے اور اگر اس سے کم ہوں تو بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے۔ پس شرط یہ ہے کہ کسی کا حصہ ساتویں سے کم نہ ہو ورنہ پھر کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ وصف قربت مفقود ہو گیا لہذا ایک گائے میں اگر آٹھ آدمی شریک ہوں تو کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Ruling of sacrificing a big animal on behalf of less than seven persons. And it is permissible for five or six or three. Muhammad mentioned this in al-Asl, because when it is permissible for seven, then for fewer is more fitting. And it is not permissible for eight, following the qiyas in matters where there is no text. Likewise, if the share of one of them is less than one-seventh, it is not permissible for all, due to the absence of the attribute of worship (qurbah) in some. And we will explain this if Allah wills. Translation: And it is permissible (the cow or camel) for five or six, as Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut, because when it is permissible for seven, then for fewer is more fitting. And it is not permissible for eight, following qiyas in matters where there is no text. Likewise, if the share of one of them is less than one-seventh, it is not permissible for all, because the attribute of qurbah is absent in some. And we will explain this soon if Allah wills. Explanation: Sharing a big animal among seven persons is permissible, and if fewer than seven, it is even more permissible. So the condition is that no one's share is less than one-seventh; otherwise, no one's qurbani will be valid because the attribute of qurbah is lost. Thus, if eight persons share a cow, no one's qurbani is valid.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage extends the earlier ruling. Since a big animal can be shared by up to seven persons, it logically follows that sharing among fewer (like five, six, or three) is also permissible. This is based on qiyas a min al-adna (argument from the lesser to the greater). However, sharing among more than seven (e.g., eight) is not permissible, because there is no textual evidence (nass) allowing it, so qiyas on the principle that the act of worship is one act per animal would disallow it. Additionally, even if the number is seven or fewer, it is a condition that each participant's share must be at least one-seventh of the animal. If any person's share is less than that (e.g., because someone takes a smaller portion), then the sacrifice is invalid for all, because the attribute of qurbah (the devotional aspect) is missing for that person whose share is deficient. The commentator promises to elaborate later. This highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the share being substantial enough to constitute a valid act of worship.

Key Terms
وصف القربت (wasf al-qurbah): The attribute of being an act of worship; here it refers to the validity of the sacrifice as a devotional act. If a share is too small, it lacks this attribute.
بدرجہ اولی (bi-darajat ula): A principle of legal reasoning: what is permissible for a larger number is even more permissible for a smaller number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible for all eight.
B) It is permissible only if they are from the same household.
C) It is not permissible for any of them.
D) It is permissible with dislike (makruh).

Key Takeaway
Sharing a cow or camel for qurbani is valid only if the number does not exceed seven and every share is at least one-seventh of the animal.

Imam Malik's View on Qurbani per Household: A Hanafi Refutation
Presents and refutes Imam Malik's view that qurbani is per household per year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Maliki position on qurbani per household and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith 'upon every household' as referring to the head of the household.

Core Idea
A single sheep cannot cover an entire household; the hadith refers to the head of the household.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute over the obligation of qurbani. Imam Malik holds that a single sheep suffices for an entire household, citing a hadith about 'every household.' The Hanafi school, represented in al-Hidayah, refutes this by interpreting the hadith as referring to the head of the household (qayyim). Understanding this dispute clarifies the individual nature of the obligation and the rules for sharing sacrificial animals.

Guided Path
1
State the Maliki position and its dalil
Identify Imam Malik's ruling that one sheep is valid for an entire household, even if more than seven, and not valid for two households even if less than seven. Note his proof: the hadith 'Upon every household every year is an udhiyah and atirah.'
The Maliki view takes the hadith literally.
2
Identify the Hanafi interpretation of the same hadith
The Hanafi author responds that the term 'household' (ahl bayt) actually refers to the head of the household (qayyim), the one with wealth. This interpretation is supported by another hadith: 'Upon every Muslim every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' Thus, the obligation is individual, not collective.
Hanafis use a contextual reading (qira'ah) to specify the general term.
3
Examine the supporting evidence for the Hanafi view
The supporting hadith ('upon every Muslim') explicitly makes the obligation individual. This indicates that the first hadith must be interpreted in line with the second, not contradicting it.
The Hanafi principle of interpreting general (amm) texts in light of specific (khass) texts is at play.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis require each eligible individual to sacrifice or share a big animal (up to seven). Malikis allow one small animal for the whole household. This affects families with multiple eligible members.
The difference arises from how each school defines the obligated entity.
5
Understand the subsidiary ruling on sharing a camel
The passage also states that sharing a camel in halves (two individuals) is permissible, even though the standard share is 1/7. This is because half of 1/7 (i.e., more than 1/7) is valid by subsidiary reasoning.
This shows Hanafi flexibility in share calculations when partners agree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام مالک کا نقطہ نظر
وقال مالك تجوز عن اهل بيت واحد وان كانوا اكثر من سبعة ولا تجوز عن اهل بيتين وان كانوا اقل منها لقوله عليه السلام على كل اهل بيت فى كل عام اضحاة وعتيرة قلنا المراد منه والله اعلم قيم اهل البيت لان اليسارله يؤيده ما يروى على كل مسلم في كل عام اضحاة وعتيرة ولو كانت البدنة بين اثنين نصفين تجوز فى الاصح لانه لما جاز ثلثة الاسباع جاز نصف السبع تبع
ترجمہ اور مالک نے فرمایا جائز ہے ایک گھر والوں کی طرف سے اگر چہ وہ سات سے زیادہ ہوں اور دو گھر والوں سے جائز نہیں اگر چہ وہ سات سے کم ہوں۔ نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ ہر گھر والوں پر ہر سال قربانی اور عتیرہ ہے تو ہم کہیں گے کہ مراد اس سے واللہ اعلم گھر والوں کا منتظم ہے اس لئے کہ مالداری اس کے لئے ہے موید ہے اس کی وہ حدیث جو مروی ہے کہ ہر مسلمان پر ہر سال میں ایک قربانی اور عتیرہ ہے اور اگر اونٹ دو آدمیوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہو تو اصح قول کے مطابق جائز ہے اس لئے کہ جب سات میں سے تین حصے جائز ہیں تو اس کی تبعیت میں ساتویں حصے کا نصف جائز ہوگا۔
تشریح امام مالک کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ ایک بکری ایک گھر کی طرف سے تو ہو سکتی ہے اگر چہ وہ گھر والے سات سے زیادہ بھی ہوں اور ایک بکری وہ گھر والوں کی طرف سے نہیں ہوسکتی اگر چہ وہ سات سے کم ہوں۔ اور اس حدیث سے استدلال کرتے ہیں جو یہاں مذکور ہے۔ اولاً تو یہ حدیث متکلم ہے اور بعد ثبوت صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کا جواب دیا کہ گھر کا منتظم مراد ہے اور قربانی فقط اس کی طرف سے ہوگی کیونکہ اس پر واجب ہے اس لئے کہ مالدار وہی ہے اس کے اور بھی مختلف جوابات دیئے گئے ہیں۔
Imam Malik's viewpoint: And Malik said: It is permissible for one household (ahl bayt) even if they are more than seven, and not permissible for two households even if they are less than seven, due to his (saw) saying: 'Upon every household (ahl bayt) every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' We say: What is meant by it, and Allah knows best, is the head of the household (qayyim ahl al-bayt), because wealth is his. This is supported by what is narrated: 'Upon every Muslim every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' And if a camel is between two persons in halves, it is permissible according to the soundest view (al-asahh), because when three-sevenths are permissible, then half of a seventh is permissible as a subsidiary. Translation: And Malik said: It is permissible for one household even if they are more than seven, and not permissible for two households even if they are less than seven, because of the Prophet's saying: 'Upon every household every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' We will say: What is meant by it, and Allah knows best, is the head of the household (qayyim), because wealth is for him. This is supported by the hadith narrated: 'Upon every Muslim every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' And if a camel is between two persons in halves, it is permissible according to the soundest view, because when three-sevenths are permissible, then half of a seventh is permissible as a subsidiary. Explanation: Imam Malik's school is that one sheep can be for one household even if the household has more than seven members, and one sheep cannot be for two households even if they are less than seven. He argues from the hadith mentioned. Firstly, this hadith is disputed (mutakallam), and after its authenticity, the author of al-Hidayah responded that what is meant is the head of the household, and the qurbani is only on his behalf because he is the one obligated as he is wealthy. Other different answers have also been given.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents a difference of opinion between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the permissibility of sharing qurbani animals. Imam Malik holds that a single sheep can suffice for an entire household (ahl bayt) no matter how many members, even if more than seven, based on the hadith 'Upon every household every year is an udhiyah and atirah.' Conversely, he does not allow a single sheep for two separate households even if they total less than seven. The Hanafi commentator (author of al-Hidayah) responds by interpreting the hadith differently: the 'household' mentioned refers to the head of the household (qayyim al-bayt), i.e., the one who is financially responsible. This is supported by another hadith that mentions 'every Muslim' individually. Thus, qurbani is obligatory on each eligible Muslim individually, not collectively per household. The passage also addresses a related issue: if two persons share a camel in halves, it is permissible according to the sounder view (al-asahh), because if three-sevenths of a camel can be valid (as in a seven-person share), then half of one-seventh (which is more than 1/7) is permissible as a subsidiary. This shows Hanafi consistency regarding minimum share requirements.

Key Terms
قیم اہل البیت (qayyim ahl al-bayt): The head of the household who is financially responsible (the one who provides for the family). In context, the one upon whom qurbani is obligatory.
عتیرہ (atirah): A pre-Islamic practice of sacrificing an animal during Rajab, later abrogated; mentioned in the hadith to emphasize the obligation of udhiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, what does the phrase 'ahl bayt' in the hadith refer to?
A) All members of the household collectively
B) The head of the household (qayyim)
C) The children of the household
D) The guests of the household

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith 'upon every household' as referring to the head of the household, making qurbani an individual obligation.

Sharing a Large Sacrificial Animal Among Fewer Than Seven
States the ruling and basis for permissibility of sharing a cow/camel among five, six, or three persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing a cow or camel among fewer than seven persons and explain the qiyas awla basis.

Core Idea
A large animal may be shared by five, six, or three, but not eight, because each share must be at least one-seventh.

The Qur'an and Sunnah permit sharing a large sacrificial animal among seven persons. The Hanafi school extends this permissibility to fewer than seven using a fortiori analogy (qiyas awla). However, this extension has a strict condition: no one's share may be less than one-seventh of the animal. This lesson explains the ruling, its proof, and the critical condition that preserves the sacrificial validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sharing a cow or camel for udhiyah (sacrifice) among multiple persons. The text states it is permissible (jā'iz) for five, six, or three persons, but not for eight.
The ruling is permissibility (sahih) under the condition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy) based on the established ruling for seven persons, which is derived from the Sunnah (hadith of Jabir in Sahih Muslim).
Qiyas awla is a stronger form of analogy where the secondary case is more deserving of the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The text argues: if it is permissible for seven (the original case), then it is even more appropriate (awlā) for fewer than seven because the share size is larger, making the act of worship stronger.
This reasoning is explicit in the phrase 'bidarajah al-ulā'.
4
Note the condition
The permissibility is conditional upon each person's share being at least one-seventh of the animal. If any share is less (e.g., eight persons or one person takes less than 1/7), the sacrifice is invalid for all because the 'attribute of closeness' (wasf al-qurbah) is lost.
This condition is derived from the requirement that each share must be sufficient to be a valid act of worship.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Imam Mālik reportedly holds a different view, though the details are not given in this passage.
Other schools may have different conditions; this lesson focuses on the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الأضحية
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدا به جلد - ۱۳
سات سے کم آدمیوں کی طرف سے بڑے جانور کی قربانی کا حکم
وتجوز عن خمسة اوستة او ثلثة ذكره محمد فى الاصل لانه لما جاز عن سبعة فعمن دونهم أولى ولا تجوز عن ثمانية اخذا بالقياس فيما لا نص فيه وكذا اذا كان نصيب احدهم اقل من السبع لا يجوز عن الكل لانعدام وصف القربة فى البعض و نبین ه ان شاء تعالی ترجمہ اور جائز ہے یہ گائے اور اونٹ) پانچ یا چھ کی طرف سے اس کو محد نے مبسوط میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب کہ جائز ہے یہ سات کی طرف سے تو سات سے کم کی طرف سے بدرجہ اولی ، اور جائز نہیں ہے آٹھ کی طرف سے قیاس پر عمل کرتے ہوئے اس کے بارے میں جس کے سلسلہ میں نص نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ ان میں سے ایک کا حصہ ساتویں سے کم ہو تو کل کی طرف سے جائز نہ ہوگی بعض کے اندر وصف قربت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ہم انشاء اللہ اس کو عنقریب بیان کریں گے۔
تشریح بڑے جانور میں سے سات آدمیوں کی شرکت جائز ہے اور اگر اس سے کم ہوں تو بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے۔ پس شرط یہ ہے کہ کسی کا حصہ ساتویں سے کم نہ ہو ورنہ پھر کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ وصف قربت مفقود ہو گیا لہذا ایک گائے میں اگر آٹھ آدمی شریک ہوں تو کسی کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
The Book of Sacrifice. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume 13. Ruling on sacrifice of a large animal on behalf of less than seven persons. 'And it is permissible on behalf of five or six or three; Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl. Because when it is permissible on behalf of seven, then on behalf of less than them is more appropriate. And it is not permissible on behalf of eight, by way of qiyas in matters where there is no text. Likewise, if the share of one of them is less than one-seventh, it is not permissible on behalf of all due to the absence of the attribute of closeness (qurbah) in some. And we will explain it, if Allah wills.' Translation: It is permissible for a cow/camel on behalf of five or six; Muhammad mentioned it in al-Mabsut. Because when it is permissible for seven, then for less than seven is even more appropriate. And it is not permissible for eight, acting on qiyas where there is no text. Likewise, when one person's share is less than one-seventh, it is not permissible for all because the attribute of closeness is absent in some. And we will soon explain it, if Allah wills. Explanation: Sharing a large animal among seven persons is permissible, and if less than that, it is even more appropriate. So the condition is that no one's share is less than one-seventh; otherwise, no one's sacrifice will be permissible because the attribute of closeness is lost. Hence, if eight persons share a cow, none of their sacrifices will be permissible.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof: The permissibility of sharing a cow or camel among fewer than seven persons is established by Imam Muhammad's report in his book al-Asl (which is part of Zahir al-Riwayah). The reasoning is qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy): if it is permissible for seven, it is even more so for less than seven. However, this permissibility has a condition: each person's share must be at least one-seventh of the animal. If any share is less, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the required 'attribute of closeness to Allah' (qurbah) is absent in that deficient share. The text also clarifies that eight persons are not permissible, as per qiyas (since it would reduce shares below one-seventh). This ruling is a direct application of the Hanafi method: where there is explicit text (for seven), qiyas awla extends it to fewer; where there is no text, qiyas prevents extension to more.

Key Terms
وصف القربة (wasf al-qurbah): The attribute of being a means of drawing closer to Allah; the sacrificial intention and validity.
بدرجہ اولی (bi darajah al-ula): A fortiori; even more appropriate or preferable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum permissible share for each person when sharing a cow for sacrifice?
A) One-fifth of the animal
B) One-seventh of the animal
C) One-eighth of the animal
D) There is no minimum; any share is acceptable

Key Takeaway
A cow or camel may be shared by up to seven persons for sacrifice, and fewer than seven are even more appropriate, provided each person's share is at least one-seventh.
