Days of Sacrifice: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of sacrifice days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the days of sacrifice and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence.

Core Idea
When evidence conflicts, Hanafis take the certain minimum (3 days) over a literal reading of 'all days'.

How many days does Islam allow for sacrifice? The Hanafi school limits it to three days (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah), while the Shafi'i school permits four (10th-13th). This difference stems from how each school handles conflicting hadith reports and the principle of precaution (ihtiyat). In this lesson, we examine the proofs and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the number of permissible days for sacrifice.
Hanafi: 3 days; Shafi'i: 4 days.
2
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
Analyze the hadith 'The days of Tashriq are all days of sacrifice' and understand why it is used as evidence.
Shafi'i relies on a general hadith.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze the report from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas that 'the days of Nahr are three, the best is the first.' Understand why it is considered stronger (hearing from the Prophet, not opinion).
Hanafi relies on specific Companion reports.
4
Understand the Hanafi usul principle
Learn the principle of taking the certain minimum (al-mutaqayyan) when reports conflict, and how it leads to the Hanafi position.
Precaution (ihtiyat) requires taking the less extensive option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وهى جائزة فى ثلثة ايام يوم النحر ويومان بعده وقال الشافعى ثلثة ايام بعده لقوله عليه السلام ايام التشريق كلها ايام ذبح ولنا ماروى عن عمر و على و ابن عباس رضى الله عنهم قالوا ايام النحر ثلثة افضلها اولها وقد قالوه سماعا لان الراى لا يهتدى الى المقادير وفى الاخبار تعارض فاخذنا بالمتيقن وهو الاقل وافضلها اولها كما قالوا ولان فيه مسارعة الى اداء القربة وهو الأصل الالمعارض ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور قربانی جائز ہے تین دنوں میں یوم نحر میں اور اس کے بعد دو دنوں میں اور فرمایا شافعی نے یوم نحر کے بعد تین نوں تک نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ ایام تشریق کل کے کل ذبح کے ایام ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو عمر اور علی اور ابن عباس سے مروی ہے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ ایام نحرتین دن میں ان میں سے افضل پہلا دن ہے اور انہوں نے یہ بات سن کر کہی ہے اس لئے کہ رائے مقادیر کی جانب رہنمائی نہیں پاتی اور اخبار میں تعارض ہے تو ہم نے متین کو لیا اور وہ اقل ہے اور ان میں سے افضل ان میں کا پہلا دن ہے جیسا کہ ان حضرات نے فرمایا ہے (صحابہ ثلاثہ نے ) اور اس لئے کہ اس میں اداء قربت کی جانب پیش قدمی ہے اور یہی اصل سے مگر کسی معارض کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح ابھی عید گاہ میں نماز نہیں ہوئی اور مسجد میں ہوگئی تو قربانی جائز ہوگی۔ یہ استحسان ہے کیوں کہ یہ معتبر نماز ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے بر عکس ہو تو وہ بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے اور بقول بعض قیاس اور استحسانا ہر اعتبار سے جائز ہے۔ تنبیہ فجر اور ظہر میں تا خیر معارض کی وجہ سے ہے جیسے اسفر و ابالفجر فانه اعظم للاجر ، اور جیسے ابردوا بالظهرفان شدة الحر من فيح جهنم.
He (al-Quduri) said: It (sacrifice) is permissible in three days: the day of Nahr and two days after it. Al-Shafi'i said: three days after it, due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'The days of Tashriq are all days of sacrifice.' And for us is what was narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) that they said: 'The days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first.' And they said it by hearing (from the Prophet) because opinion cannot reach to measures. And there is conflict among the reports, so we took the certain (al-mutaqayyan) which is the least. And the best is the first, as they said. And because in it there is hastening to perform the act of worship, and that is the original principle when there is no contrary evidence.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The matn states the Hanafi position: sacrifice is allowed on three days: 10th Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr) and the two following days (11th and 12th). Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is allowed on four days: 10th and the three days after (10th, 11th, 12th, 13th). The Shafi'i evidence is the hadith 'all days of Tashriq are days of sacrifice.' The Hanafi evidence is the statement of 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas that 'the days of Nahr are three, the best is the first.' Since this is a matter of numerical limits not reached by analogy, the Companions must have heard it from the Prophet. Moreover, when reports conflict, we take the certain minimum (3 days) rather than the Shafi'i expansion. The first day is best for hastening to worship. The tanbih (note) explains that delaying acts of worship may be due to some benefit, like delaying Fajr prayer for isfar (clear dawn) or Zuhr in extreme heat, but here no such benefit delays sacrifice.

Key Terms
یوم نحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrificing the animals.
ایام تشریق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Yawm al-Nahr: 11th, 12th, 13th.
متین / متیقن (mutayyaqin / mutayyan): The certain minimum: in case of conflicting evidence, the certain number of days is taken (3 days).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah
B) 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah
C) Only 10th of Dhul Hijjah
D) 9th, 10th, and 11th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts sacrifice to three days (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah) based on Companion reports and the usul principle of taking the certain minimum when evidence conflicts.

Ruling on Night Slaughter
Ruling and karaha for slaughtering at night during sacrifice days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering at night during the days of Nahr and explain why it is makruh.

Core Idea
Night slaughter is valid but disliked due to risk of error; the sacrifice days are three, with the 13th being tashriq only.

The permissibility of sacrifice during the festival is generally known, but what about slaughtering at night? This passage clarifies that while it is permissible, there is a subtle legal detestation due to the potential for mistakes in darkness. Additionally, it defines which days qualify for sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first part of the passage to determine what act is being ruled and what the legal classification (hukm) is. Note that it says 'ja'iz' (permissible) but 'makruh' (disliked).
The act is slaughtering the sacrificial animal at night during the days of Nahr.
2
Understand the reason for karaha
The passage gives the illah (reason) for the dislike: the possibility of error in darkness. Consider why this makes it makruh tanzihi rather than makruh tahrimi.
Error could include missing the correct spot or injuring the animal improperly.
3
Differentiate the days of Nahr and Tashriq
The passage explains that the days of Nahr (sacrifice) are three and the days of Tashriq (drying meat) are three, overlapping across four calendar days. Identify which days are exclusive or shared.
10th: only Nahr; 13th: only Tashriq; 11th and 12th: both.
4
Apply the ruling to night slaughter
Combine the two parts: night slaughter is allowed on the nights of the three valid sacrifice days (10th–12th nights) but is disliked. Slaughter on the night of the 13th is not part of the sacrifice period.

Source Text

And slaughter is permissible in their nights, but it is makruh due to the possibility of error in the darkness of the night. The days of Nahr are three, and the days of Tashriq are three, and all pass with four: the first is only Nahr, the last is only Tashriq, and the two middle ones are both Nahr and Tashriq.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on slaughtering during the nights of the sacrifice days. It is permissible (ja'iz) but makruh (disliked) because of the risk of error in darkness. The commentary then clarifies the classification of the days: the 10th is exclusively Yawm al-Nahr (sacrifice), the 13th is exclusively Yawm al-Tashriq (drying meat, no sacrifice), and the two middle days (11th and 12th) are both Nahr and Tashriq, meaning sacrifice and drying meat are both valid. The overall period spans four days (10th-13th) but only the first three are for sacrifice.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; the act is valid but one should avoid it due to potential error.
یوم تشریق (yawm al-tashriq): Day of drying the meat; 13th is exclusively tashriq, not for sacrifice.

Sacrifice Better than Its Value in Charity: Ruling and Rationale
Ruling with rational proof: sacrifice > charity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that performing the sacrifice is superior to donating its monetary value, and identify the key rational proof (qiyas) used.

Core Idea
Sacrifice is superior to charity because it is a time-bound obligatory/emphasized sunnah act, whereas charity given in its place is merely voluntary.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common question: which is better — to sacrifice an animal or give the equivalent in charity? The Hanafi school unequivocally prefers the ritual act itself. In this lesson, we will unpack the two rational proofs (dalil aqli) that the author presents and see how they establish the superiority of the prescribed worship over a monetary substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being compared: sacrificing an animal (dhabh) vs. giving its monetary value in charity (sadaqah). The ruling is that sacrifice is afdal (better).
2
Examine the first proof: legal nature
Compare the legal status: sacrifice is wajib (Abu Hanifa) or sunnah mu'akkadah (Sahibayn); charity given in its place is pure tatawwu' (voluntary). Since an obligatory or emphasized sunnah act is superior to a voluntary one, sacrifice is better.
This holds regardless of the wajib/sunnah dispute within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the second proof: time-binding
Sacrifice has a fixed time (Eid days) and is lost if that time passes; charity can be performed at any time. This time-sensitivity elevates the ritual.
The loss of opportunity makes the act irreplaceable.
4
Note the analogy (qiyas)
The text likens sacrifice to tawaf and prayer — acts that cannot be substituted with money. The illa (effective cause) is that these are specific acts of worship with fixed times and rituals; their spiritual benefit is unique and cannot be replaced by monetary equivalent.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) using qiyas.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dimensions
The Hanafi position is that sacrifice is afdal; other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow substitution with charity if one cannot perform. Within Hanafi, the superiority ruling is consistent whether sacrifice is considered wajib or sunnah mu'akkadah.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that sacrifice is superior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتضحية فيها افضل من التصدق بثمن الاضحية لانها تقع واجبة أوستة والتصدق تطوع محض فتفضل عليه ولانها تفوت بقوات وقتها والصدقة توتى بها في الاوقات كلها فنزلت منزلة الطواف والصلوة في
And performing the sacrifice is better than giving charity with its price, because it occurs as obligatory or sunnah, while charity is pure supererogation, so it surpasses it. And because it is lost at the end of its time, while charity can be given at all times. So it takes the rank of tawaf and prayer in...
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling and rationale: actual sacrifice (al-dhabh) is superior to giving the value of the animal in charity. The reason is that sacrifice is either wajib (obligatory) or sunnah mu'akkada (emphasized sunnah) – depending on the view – whereas charity given as a substitute is purely voluntary (tatawwu' mahd). Moreover, sacrifice has a specific time window; if missed, the opportunity is lost, whereas charity can be performed at any time. Therefore, sacrifice is analogous to tawaf and prayer, which cannot be substituted by monetary equivalent. This establishes the superiority of the ritual act over its financial equivalent.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): Obligatory; for qurbani, some Hanafi views consider it wajib (as per Abu Hanifa) or sunnah mu'akkadah (as per Sahibayn).
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship; here referring to charity given freely without obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because sacrifice is an obligatory or sunnah act, while charity as substitute is purely voluntary.
C) Because sacrifice can be done at any time, unlike charity.
D) Because the animal meat is more nutritious.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that performing the sacrifice is superior to donating its value because it is a time-bound act of worship with a higher legal status (wajib/sunnah mu'akkadah), unlike charity which is purely voluntary.

Superiority of Qurbani Over Sadaqah: An Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Explaining why sacrificing is superior to giving its value in charity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the superiority of sacrifice over charity and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether sacrifice is wajib or sunnah.

Core Idea
Sacrifice outperforms charity because its time is limited and its legal status is wajib/sunnah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses a key question: is it better to slaughter an animal during Eid al-Adha or to give its value in charity? The author argues for the superiority of sacrifice, grounding his reasoning in two arguments—the higher legal status of sacrifice (wajib or sunnah) over voluntary charity, and the time-sensitivity of the act. The passage also highlights the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (wajib) and the Sahibayn (sunnah). We will examine both arguments and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Claim
The author states that sacrificing during the days of Nahr is better than giving the price as charity. This is the main thesis.
The claim is not about absolute superiority of sacrifice over all charity, but specifically during the prescribed days.
2
Extract the First Argument: Legal Status
Sacrifice is either wajib (per Zahir al-Riwayah) or sunnah (per Sahibayn), while charity is merely nafl (voluntary). A wajib or sunnah act is inherently higher than a nafl act.
The author uses 'either' to cover both positions, showing the argument holds regardless of the dispute.
3
Extract the Second Argument: Time Specificity
Sacrifice can only be performed during the specific days of Nahr; if missed, the opportunity is lost. Charity can be given at any time. Therefore, the sacrifice has a unique urgency.
This argument emphasizes the restricted window, making the act more valuable.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The passage mentions that in Zahir al-Riwayah sacrifice is wajib, while the Sahibayn consider it sunnah. Note that this dispute does not affect the superiority conclusion—both statuses are above nafl.
The author presents the dispute neutrally, not favoring one over the other for the purpose of this argument.
5
Understand the Tawaf Analogy
The case of sacrifice for a non-Makki (Afaqi) is compared to tawaf vs. nafl prayer. Tawaf can only be done in Mecca, while prayer can be offered anywhere. Similarly, sacrifice is tied to a specific time, making it superior to charity.
This analogy reinforces the time-sensitivity argument.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
حق الافاقی
كتاب الاصحية.
ترجمہ اور ایام نحر میں قربانی کرنا قربانی کی قیمت صدقہ کرنے سے افضل ہے اسلئے کہ قربانی واجب واقع ہوگی یا سنت اور تصدق محض صدقہ ہے تو وہ (قربانی کرنا ) فوقیت رکھے گا اس پر ( تطوع پر ) اور اس لئے کہ قربانی فوت ہو جاتی ہے اس کے وقت کے فوات سے اور صدقہ کو ادا کیا جا سکتا ہے تمام اوقات میں تو اتار لیا جائے گا قربانی کو آفاقی کے حق میں طواف اور نماز کے درجہ میں ۔ تشریح ظاہر الروایہ میں قربانی واجب ہے اور بقول صاحبین سنت ہے اور صدقہ محض تطوع اور نفل ہے اور واجب اور سنت تطوع محض سے عمدہ اور بلند ہوتے ہیں لہذا ایام نحر میں قربانی افضل ہے قربانی کی قیمت کا صدقہ کرنے سے بوجہ دلیل مذکور ۔ نیز صدقہ تو جب چاہو کر سکتے ہو اور قربانی کے لئے یہی ایام مخصوص ہیں تو اس کا مسئلہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے آفاقی کے حق میں طواف اور نفلی نماز کا مسئلہ ہے کہ طواف افضل ہے کیونکہ طواف تو صرف یہیں کر سکتا ہے اور نماز ہندوستان جا کر بھی جتنی چاہے پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
And during the days of Nahr, sacrificing is better than giving the price of the sacrifice as charity because the sacrifice either becomes obligatory (wajib) or sunnah, while charity is merely voluntary sadaqah. So it (sacrificing) has superiority over it (voluntary charity). And because the sacrifice is lost when its time passes, while charity can be given at all times. So sacrificing is lifted to the level of tawaf and prayer for the Afaqi (non-Makki). Explanation: In Zahir al-Riwayah, sacrifice is wajib, and according to the Sahibayn it is sunnah. Charity is merely voluntary and nafl. Wajib and sunnah are higher and better than mere voluntary acts. Therefore, during the days of Nahr, sacrificing is better than giving the price of the sacrifice in charity due to the mentioned reason. Also, charity you can give whenever you want, but sacrifice is specific to these days. So its case becomes like the case of tawaf and nafl prayer for an Afaqi: tawaf is better because it can only be performed here (in Mecca), while prayer can be performed in India as much as one wants.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage explains the superiority of physically sacrificing an animal during the days of Nahr over giving its monetary value in charity. The author first states that sacrificing is better, providing two reasons: (1) Sacrifice is either wajib (per Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Abu Hanifa) or sunnah (per Sahibayn), whereas charity is merely nafl. A wajib or sunnah act is inherently superior to a nafl act. (2) The time for sacrifice is limited; once the days of Nahr pass, the opportunity is lost. Charity, however, can be given at any time. The author then draws an analogy: for a non-Makki (Afaqi) pilgrim, tawaf is better than nafl prayer because tawaf can only be done in Mecca, while prayer can be offered anywhere. Similarly, sacrifice is better because its time is restricted. The passage also highlights the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the status of sacrifice: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn) consider it sunnah. Despite this difference, both agree that sacrifice is superior to charity.

Key Terms
قربانی (qurbani): The ritual sacrifice of an animal during the days of Eid al-Adha.
آفاقی (afaqi): A person who does not reside in Mecca (outside the Haram boundaries).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is sacrificing an animal during the days of Nahr better than giving its value in charity?
A) Because sacrifice is wajib and charity is haram.
B) Because sacrifice has a specific limited time while charity can be done anytime.
C) Because charity is only for the poor.
D) Because sacrifice is always wajib.

Key Takeaway
Sacrifice is superior to charity due to its higher legal status and time-sensitivity, regardless of the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether it is wajib or sunnah.

Ruling on Missing the Time for Sacrifice
Stating the ruling for one who misses the days of Nahr without sacrificing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wajib compensation when the days of Nahr pass without sacrificing, and apply the Hanafi qiyas to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
A missed obligatory sacrifice is not dropped; it must be compensated by sadaqah, just as Jumu'ah is made up as Zuhr.

When a person is obligated to sacrifice but fails to do so before the end of the three days of Nahr, the obligation does not simply vanish. Instead, Hanafi fiqh prescribes a compensatory sadaqah, analogized to the makeup of Jumu'ah. The specific compensation depends on whether the person is rich or poor, and the conditions under which the sacrifice became obligatory. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its justification through qiyas jaliy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the compensation for a missed obligatory sacrifice. The ruling is that sadaqah is wajib.
The sacrifice itself was originally wajib; now the time has passed.
2
Distinguish between rich and poor
For a rich person, the obligation is due to his wealth, so he gives the value of a sheep in charity. For a poor person, the obligation arises only if he bought an animal with the intention of sacrifice during the days of Nahr; then he gives the live animal in charity.
A poor person who never bought an animal is not obligated at all.
3
Locate the qiyas (analogy)
The text draws an analogy with Jumu'ah (missed Jumu'ah is made up as Zuhr) and with fasting (fidyah when unable). The common illa is that a time-specific wajib act was missed.
This is qiyas jaliy because the illa is clearly identified.
4
Note the additional conditions from the tanbih
If a poor person gives the live animal in charity during the days of Nahr itself, he still owes a sacrifice (because slaughter is wajib). Also, for the poor, the obligation to sacrifice only arises if the animal was bought within the days of Nahr with intention.
These are important practical details.
5
Derive the final mufta bihi
Compensation by sadaqah is wajib on both rich and poor who were obligated. The amount differs as stated.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قربانی واجب تھی اور ایام قربانی گذر گئے اور قربانی نہیں کی تو کیا کرے
ولو لم يضح حتى مضت ايام النحر ان كان اوجب على نفسه او كان فقيراً وقد اشترى الاضحية تصدق بها حية وان كان غنيا تصدق بقيمة شاة اشترى اولم يشتر لانها واجبة على الغنى وتجب على الفقير بالشراء بنية التضحية عندنا فاذا فات الوقت يجب عليه التصدق اخر اجاله عن العهدة كالجمعة تقضى بعد فواتها ظهرا والصوم بعد العجز فدية
ترجمہ اور اگر قربانی نہیں کی یہاں تک کہ ایام نحر گذر گئے تو اگر اس نے اپنے اوپر قربانی واجب کی ہو یا وہ فقیر ہو اور اس نے قربانی خریدی ہو تو وہ اس کا زندہ کا صدقہ کر دے گا اور اگر مالدار ہو تو بکری کی قیمت کا صدقہ کرے گا۔ قربانی خریدی ہو یا نہ خریدی ہو۔ اسلئے کہ قربانی مالدار پر واجب ہے اور فقیر پر خریدنے سے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ قربانی کی نیت سے ہمارے نزدیک پس جب کہ وقت فوت ہو گیا تو اس پر صدقہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اپنے کو ذمہ داری سے نکالنے کے لئے جیسے جمعہ اس کے فوات کے بعد ظہر کی قضاء کی جاتی ہے اور روزہ کی قضاء کی جاتی ہے بجز کے بعد فد پہ ہے۔ تشریح مالدار پر اپنی مالداری کی وجہ سے قربانی واجب ہے اور فقیر پر جب واجب ہے کہ وہ ایام نحر میں بنیت قربانی کا جانور خریدے یا کوئی قربانی کی نذر کرے تو اس پر بھی واجب ہے۔ بہر حال قربانی واجب تھی اور ایام قربانی گذر گئے اور اس نے قربانی نہیں کی تو کیا کرے۔ تو فرمایا کہ اگر مالدار ہے تو ایک بکری کی قیمت کا صدقہ کرے اور اگر فقیر ہے تو زندہ بکری کا صدقہ کرنا ضروری ہے کیوں کہ قربانی ان پر واجہ تھی اور اب اگر قربانی کا وقت ختم ہو گیا تو اس کے علاوہ چارہ کار نہیں ہے۔ جیسے فوات جمعہ کے بعد ظہر کی قضاء ہوتی ہے اور فوات صوم کے بعد عاجزی کے وقت فدیہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔
تنبیہ - ایام قربانی میں زندہ بکری صدقہ کر دی تو دوسری قربانی واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ اس پر خون بہانا واجب ہے۔ شامی ص ۲۰۳ ج ۵ ۔

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۳
تنبیه - ۲ فقیر جب قربانی کا جانور بہ نیت قربانی ایام محر میں خریدے گا تو قربانی واجب ہوگی ورنہ ایام نحر سے پہلے خریدنے میں واجب نہ ہو گی ، شامی ص ۲۰۴ ج ۵ ۔ اور ہم نے اس پر احکام قربانی میں بسط سے گفتگو کی ہے۔
What should be done if sacrifice was obligatory and the days of sacrifice passed without sacrificing? And if he did not sacrifice until the days of Nahr passed: if he had obligated it upon himself, or he was poor and had bought the sacrificial animal, he should give it in charity while it is alive. And if he is rich, he should give the value of a sheep in charity, whether he had bought [an animal] or not. Because sacrifice is obligatory upon the rich, and upon the poor it becomes obligatory by purchase with the intention of sacrifice, in our view. So when the time is lost, it is obligatory upon him to give charity to free himself from liability, like Jumu'ah which is made up as Zuhr after its time is lost, and like fasting which is compensated with fidyah when one is unable. Explanation: Sacrifice is obligatory upon the rich because of his wealth, and upon the poor it becomes obligatory if he buys an animal in the days of Nahr with the intention of sacrifice, or if he vows a sacrifice. In any case, the sacrifice was obligatory and the days passed without sacrificing. So the ruling is that if he is rich, he should give the value of a sheep in charity; if he is poor, he must give the live animal in charity because the obligation was upon them, and now that the time is lost, there is no alternative. Like after the loss of Jumu'ah, Zuhr is offered as makeup, and after the loss of fasting, fidyah is obligatory when one is unable. Note: If he gave a live sheep in charity during the days of Nahr, another sacrifice becomes obligatory upon him because it is obligatory upon him to shed blood. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 203). Note 2: When a poor person buys an animal for sacrifice with intention during the days of Nahr, sacrifice becomes obligatory; otherwise, if he bought before the days of Nahr, it does not become obligatory. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 204). And we have discussed this in detail in the rulings of sacrifice.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a person was obligated to sacrifice but failed to do so before the end of the days of Nahr. The ruling distinguishes between a rich person and a poor person. For a rich person, the obligation is due to his wealth, so he must give the value of a sheep in charity. For a poor person, sacrifice only becomes obligatory if he purchased an animal with the intention of sacrifice during the prescribed days, or he vowed it; in that case, he must give the live animal itself in charity. The analogy drawn is with Jumu'ah: if one misses Jumu'ah, he prays Zuhr instead. Similarly, if one misses the obligatory sacrifice, he compensates by giving charity. The text also includes two important notes (tanbih). First, if a poor person gives the live animal in charity during the days of Nahr itself, that does not fulfill his obligation; he still owes a sacrifice because he must slaughter an animal. Second, the obligation for the poor arises only if the purchase is made within the days of Nahr with the intention of sacrifice; a purchase before those days does not trigger the obligation. These distinctions ensure the correct fulfillment of the religious duty.

Key Terms
ايام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days of Eid al-Adha (10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul-Hijjah) when sacrifice is performed.
تصدق (tasadduq): To give in charity; here it is a compulsory compensation for a missed obligatory sacrifice.
قربانی (qurbani): Sacrificial animal slaughter during Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a poor person do if the days of Nahr pass and he had bought a sacrificial animal with intention during those days?
A) He must sacrifice after the days are over.
B) He must give the live animal in charity.
C) He must give the value of the animal in charity.
D) He must fast instead.

Key Takeaway
A missed wajib sacrifice is compensated by sadaqah: the rich give the value of a sheep, the poor give the live animal (if purchased), just as missed Jumu'ah is made up with Zuhr.

Major Defects That Invalidate the Sacrificial Animal
Listing defects that invalidate udhiyah and the threshold for ear/tail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four major defects from the hadith that invalidate udhiyah, explain the Hanafi condition that the defect must be obvious (bayyin), and apply the principle that only major defects (e.g., more than half of ear/tail missing) invalidate while minor defects are excused.

Core Idea
Only major, obvious defects invalidate udhiyah; minor imperfections are automatically excused.

Sacrificial animals inevitably have small imperfections, but the Shari'ah does not demand absolute perfection. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies exactly which defects render an animal invalid and why. You will learn the four defects mentioned in the hadith, the addition of ear and tail under qiyas, and the key principle that only major defects matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four defects from the hadith
Find the four animals listed in the hadith: the clearly one-eyed, the clearly lame, the clearly sick, and the emaciated (with no marrow). Note the condition 'bayyin' (obvious) attached to each.
The hadith is quoted in the source as irrefutable proof.
2
Understand the addition of ear and tail
The text extends the list to missing ear and tail. The ear is proven by another hadith commanding to check the eye and ear; the tail is added by qiyas as it is a complete, intended organ.
This is a qiyas (analogical) expansion based on the same rationale.
3
Apply the general principle: major vs. minor defects
Animals are never free from very minor defects (e.g., a small cut). The rule is that freedom from major (fahish) defects is a condition, but minor defects are excused. This is derived from the hadith's requirement that the defect be 'obvious'.
This principle prevents unnecessary hardship in finding a perfect animal.
4
Determine the threshold for ear/tail: majority rule
If more than half of the ear or tail is missing, the animal is invalid; if half or more remains, it is valid. The majority has the ruling of the whole in both remaining and going.
There are multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on the exact threshold, but the majority rule is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the threshold
The text mentions that different narrations exist from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the precise dividing line. However, the principle of 'majority' is consistently applied.
This shows the school's flexibility in applying the principle to varying contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن عیب دار جانوروں کی قربانی جائز نہیں
قال ولا يضحى بالعمياء والعوراء والعرجاء التى لا تمشى الى المنسك ولا العجفاء لقوله عليه السلام لا تجزي في الضحايا اربعة العوراء البين عورها والعرجاء البين عرجها والمريضة البين مرضها والعجفاء التي لا تنقى قال ولا تجزى مقطوعة الاذن والذنب اما الاذن فلقوله عليه السلام استشرفوا العين والاذن اى اطلبوا اسلامتهما واما الذنب فلانه عضو كامل مقصود فصار كالاذن
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اور قربانی نہیں کرے گا اندھی کی اور نہ کانی کی اور اس لنگڑی کی جو مذبح تک نہ جا سکے اور نہ بہت دہلی کی۔ نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے ضحایا میں چار جانور جائز نہیں وہ کانی جس کا کانا پن ظاہر ہو اور وہ لنگڑی جس کا لنگڑ اپن ظاہر ہو اور وہ بیمار جس کا مرض ظاہر ہو اور وہ ڈبلی جس کا گودانہ ہو قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز نہیں کان اور ڈم گئی ۔ بہر حال کان پس نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ آنکھ اور کان کا ملاحظہ کیا کر د یعنی ان دونوں کی سلامتی دیکھا کرو اور بہر حال دم تو اس لئے کہ وہ ایک عضو کامل ہے جو مقصود ہے تو کان کے مثل ہو گیا۔
تشریح قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ معمولی عیب سے تو حیوانات خالی نہیں ہوتے تو اسلئے خالی ہونا شرط نہیں ہے البتہ عیب فاحش سے خالی ہوتے ہیں۔ تو اس سے خالی ہونا شرط ہے باقی باتیں ظاہر ہیں۔
کتنی مقدار عیب شمار کی جائے گی
قال ولا التي ذهب اكثر اذنها وذنبها وان بقى اكثر الاذن والذنب جاز لان للاكثر حكم الكل بقاء وذهب اولان العيب اليسير لا يمكن التحرز عنه فجعل عفوا -
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے وہ جانور جس کے کان اور دم کا اکثر حصہ ختم ہوا اور اگر کان اور دم کا اکثر حصہ باقی ہو تو جائز ہے اسلئے کہ بقا اور ذہاب کے اعتبار سے اکثر کے لئے کل کا حکم ہے اور عیب پیر ( معمولی عیب ) اس سے بچنا ممکن نہیں ہے تو اس کو معاف قرار
دیا جائے گا۔
تشریح معمولی عیب سے بچنا تو مشکل اور کثیر سے بچنا آسان ہے تو اگر عیب قلیل ہے تو معاف ہیں اور اگر عیب کثیر ہے تو وہ معاف نہیں اور اس کی قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی ۔ پھر قلیل و کثیر میں حد فاصل کیا ہے اس میں مختلف روایات ہیں۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے اس سلسلہ میں چار روایتیں ہیں جو ابھی آرہی ہیں۔ بقاع و ذهابا ... بقا اور باب میں اکثر کا حکم کل جیسا ہے کہ اگر اکثر حصہ باقی ہو تو گویا کل باقی ہے اور قربانی جائز ہے۔ اور اگر اکثر حصہ ختم ہو گیا ہو تو گویا کل ختم ہو گیا اور قربانی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Sacrifice is not valid with which defective animals? He said: And one should not sacrifice a blind animal, nor a one-eyed animal, nor a lame animal that cannot walk to the place of slaughter, nor an emaciated animal. Because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Four are not acceptable in sacrifices: the clearly one-eyed, the clearly lame, the clearly sick, and the emaciated that has no marrow.' He said: And an animal with a missing ear or tail is not acceptable. As for the ear, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Look to the eye and the ear' i.e., seek their soundness. As for the tail, because it is a complete organ that is intended, so it becomes like the ear. Explanation: The principle is that animals are not free from minor defects, so freedom from them is not a condition. However, freedom from major defects is a condition. The rest is clear. How much is counted as a defect? He said: And an animal whose most of its ear or tail is gone is not acceptable, but if most of the ear and tail remains, it is permissible, because the majority has the ruling of the whole in terms of remaining and going. And minor defects cannot be avoided, so they are forgiven. Explanation: Avoiding a minor defect is difficult, while avoiding a major defect is easy. So if the defect is minor, it is forgiven; if it is major, it is not forgiven, and sacrifice is not valid. Then what is the dividing line between minor and major? There are different narrations. From Imam Abu Hanifa, there are four narrations on this, which are coming later. In terms of remaining and going, the ruling of the majority is like the whole: if most remains, it is as if the whole remains, and sacrifice is valid; if most is gone, it is as if the whole is gone, and sacrifice is not valid.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage details the defects that make an animal invalid for udhiyah. It begins by listing four categories from the hadith: a blind animal, a one-eyed animal with obvious defect, a lame animal that cannot walk to the slaughter place, and an emaciated animal with no fat/marrow. These are the 'major' defects explicitly mentioned by the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam). Additionally, an animal with a missing ear or tail is also invalid. The proof for the ear is the hadith commanding to check the eye and ear; the tail is compared to the ear because it is a complete and intended organ. The commentary then establishes a general principle: animals inevitably have minor defects (like a small cut or bruise), and these are excused. However, major (fahish) defects must be absent. The text then addresses the question of how much of the ear or tail must be missing to render the animal invalid. The ruling is based on the majority: if more than half of the ear or tail is missing, the animal is invalid; if most remains, it is valid. This is because the majority takes the ruling of the whole. The text also notes that there are multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the exact threshold, but the principle of majority is the operative rule.

Key Terms
العجفاء (al-'ajfa'): An emaciated animal with no marrow/fat, so thin that it is weak.
بين (bayyin): Obvious, manifest; the defect must be clearly apparent, not subtle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid condition for an animal to be acceptable for udhiyah?
A) The animal's ear must be perfectly intact without any missing part.
B) The animal must be free from any minor defect.
C) The animal must be free from major, obvious defects.
D) The animal must not have any scar or mark.

Key Takeaway
Only major, obvious defects (blindness, one-eyed, lame unable to walk, emaciated, missing most of ear/tail) invalidate udhiyah; minor imperfections are automatically excused.
